Special Article

A Study of Korean Migration to the Northeast

(Continued from the 8th) Bin

(4) The Persecution of the Northeast Caused by Korean Migration

As described in the previous chapter, it can be seen that under the command of Japanese imperialist colonial policies, Koreans are actively migrating to our Northeast, which is flourishing. The huge amount of current migration, the broad distribution area, and the complexity of occupations, coupled with the use and direction of the Japanese, have all given our Northeast infinite persecution. Briefly described as follows.

(1) Seizing the Benefits of Paddy Fields - The harvest of paddy fields and dry fields in the Northeast is about 3 to 5 and 10, respectively. Koreans are best at planting paddy fields. Therefore, in various places along the rivers in the Northeast, the Japanese Dongtuo Company or Manchurian Financial Association lend funds to instigate pro-Japanese Koreans to go around to rent and plant paddy fields in order to monopolize the rice field business in the Northeast. According to a survey in June of this year, in Liaoning Province, such as the Hui River, Antu, Linjiang, Liu River, Zhuang River, Liaoyuan, Andong, Kangping, Benxi Lake, Shahekou, Tong River, Changbai, Heishan, Xifeng, Dongfeng, and the Yingkou, Haicheng, Taonan, Xinmin, Xingjing, and other places along the Hun River. The number of Koreans renting land to grow rice is more than 250,000. The area of paddy fields occupied is more than 2 million hectares. In Jilin, such as the Songhua, Tumen, Mudan three rivers, and the Yanji, Hunchun, Wangqing, Helong, Ningan, Dunhua, Emu, Dongning, Mishan, Tongjiang, Fujin, Mengjiang, Huachuan, Huadian, Hulin, Jilin, Changchun, Yitong, Dehui, Changling, Fuyu, Yilan, and other places in the Liao River and Yitong River basins. According to statistics, the number of Koreans growing rice is more than 300,000. The area of paddy fields occupied is about 4 million hectares. In Heilongjiang Province, such as the Black Nen River, Yangyuan, Hulan, Suihua, Hailun, Mulan Bayan, Kedong Rehe, Daohua Hulunbuir and other places in the upper and lower reaches of the Nen River and Hei River. There are about 560,000 Koreans renting land to farm. The area of paddy fields is about 150,000 hectares. In short, the footprints of Korean farmers are all over the river basins and low-lying fields in the three northeastern provinces, and the benefits of good paddy fields are almost directly and indirectly taken away by Koreans and Japanese. Not only that, the Japanese, on the one hand, instigated Koreans to rent land and cultivate in the hinterland of our Northeast, and on the other hand, they lent capital through the Mantetsu Company to vigorously encourage Koreans along the Mantetsu line to open up paddy fields, and they seized all the paddy fields cultivated by our Chinese people along the line for the use of Korean farmers. According to Japanese estimates, within three years, 300,000 hectares of paddy fields can be added along the Mantetsu line. The purpose of this active encouragement of Korean farmers to rent and cultivate farmland and open up farmland is not only to encourage Korean farmers to migrate to our country, but the most sinister thing is to use the hands of Korean farmers to buy our land and take it as their own. The harm of seizing our national power and endangering our people's food is the greatest. Secondly, over the years, Korean farmers and our Chinese farmers have created endless disputes due to the competition for water sources and rice fields. For example, the case of Korean overseas Chinese forcibly occupying civilian land and digging ditches for irrigation in Fushun County in the past, and the recent Wanbaoshan Incident, are all examples. (To be continued)

Important News

Record of the Annihilation of the Red Army by Siege at Donggu

▲ Famous Bandit Den Smashed in Ten Days

▲ Over 30,000 Bandits Captured, Over 10,000 Guns Seized

Nanchang Correspondence: The base nests of the Red bandits Zhu, Mao, Peng, and Huang in Jiangxi province are one in Ningdu and one in Donggu. The main targets of attack for the Annihilation of the Red Army are those two places. Subsequently, Ningdu was recovered. Then all efforts were made to fiercely attack Donggu. Now, a record of the battle is as follows:

▲ Situation of Donggu: Donggu is located at the border of five counties: Ji'an, Jishui, Yongfeng, Taihe, and Xingguo, about 120 li from Ji'an county town. Donggu is surrounded by many mountains, like Futian in Ji'an, Baisha and Shuinan in Jishui, Yaotian, Shaxi, and Longgang in Yongfeng, Gulonggang and Chenggang in Xingguo, and Gubei and Luojiaxu in Taihe. The terrain is dangerous. Although there are one or two narrow paths, neither carriages nor people can walk side by side. In the center, there are plains and fertile fields of several hundred li, with the Hu River winding through them, like a paradise. Since the late Ming Dynasty, it has been occupied by vagrant bandits. During the Qing Dynasty, it was once recovered. In the sixteenth year of the Republic of China, it was occupied by local bandits and mutinous soldiers such as Hu Zhusheng and Luo Binghui. At first, it was nothing more than a haven for those fleeing after robbery. The local government, due to its remote location and mutual buck-passing among the counties, refused to suppress it, leading to its growth. In the early seventeenth year, after the Hunan-Guangdong-Jiangxi armies broke through Jinggang, Zhu Mao entered Fujian from the border of Hunan and Guangdong. Their forces gradually extended from the west bank of the Gan River to the east bank, eventually concentrating in Donggu. The Red bandit pseudo-Central Executive Committee, Agricultural and Workers Bank, Military and Political School, rear hospitals, and Soviet government organs were all established in Donggu. Zhu, Mao, Peng, and Huang then brazenly used this place as the center of gravity for issuing orders, redizing the southeast, and commanding Red bandit riots in various provinces. Nearby counties also fell into a state of utter disaster.

▲ Steps of the Attack: This time, the Annihilation of the Red Army attacked Donggu with the right wing of Chen Mingshu advancing from Ji'an and Taihe, attacking its northwest; the Fifth Route Army advancing from Jishui and Yongfeng, attacking its northeast; the central route Twenty-sixth Route Army detouring its west from Ningle; and the left wing detouring its south from Ningdu, cutting off its route into Fujian. After the general offensive order was issued, Chen Mingshu's forces advanced from Futian through the border of Taihe to Xingguo, in order to converge with the left wing, first capturing Xingcheng, then taking Donggu. The Han and Hao divisions of the Fifth Route Army searched and advanced southwest after capturing Tengtian, Baisha, and Shuinan, connecting with the Jiang and Cai divisions. The central route Li Yunjie division arrived near Shaxi on the 22nd. About a division of bandit troops under Huang Gonglue was stationed there. Li's division then attacked them at dawn. Around 8:00 a.m., the battle became fierce. The bandits repeatedly launched fierce attacks on the flanks and rear of Li's division. At 12:00 noon, Li's division launched a fierce charge against the bandits. The bandits could not withstand it and retreated in succession, so they occupied Shaxi, seizing more than 400 firearms and capturing more than 1,000 bandits, including dozens of female bandits. When the remaining bandits retreated towards Longgangxu, the planes followed and dropped bombs, killing many bandits. At the same time, another unit of the left wing of the Annihilation of the Red Army recovered Longgang. After Li's division cleared out the remaining bandits in Shaxi, it continued to advance westward on the 24th. The bandits feigned retreat to the vicinity of Chiban'ao and Yuexi, using a small number of peasant bandits to hold the front, guarding the pre-built fortifications, while tens of thousands of armed bandits detoured to attack the flanks and rear of Li's division. This was again detected by the planes, which immediately dropped several bombs on the hidden main force of the Red bandits. The bombs all exploded, killing and wounding many bandits. At the same time, a communication bag was used to notify Li's division, ordering them to pay attention to the bandit's flank attack. Meanwhile, Gao Shuxun and Hao Mengling's armies were also notified to send teams to flank and attack. Each unit received the plane's report and immediately began the attack. From 7:00 a.m. to 4:00 p.m., more than 3,000 bandits were killed and 1,700-1,800 were captured in the vicinity of Yuexi. More than 3,000 rifles, more than 20 machine guns, and 18 mortars were seized. The remaining bandits scattered and fled back to Donggu. Spears, flags, and the corpses of Red bandits were everywhere. At this time, the right wing and central route of the Annihilation of the Red Army were completely connected. On the left wing, after capturing Ningdu, the main force advanced westward from Ning. Chen and Mao's divisions occupied Longgang on the 23rd, killing and capturing many bandits. Zhao's division originally advanced southwest from Ning, cutting off the route from Donggu and Xingguo through Ruijin into Fujian. On the 22nd, it recovered Gulonggang, an important place on the border of the four counties of Xing, Yu, Ning, and Rui, cutting off the connection between the bandits of Xing and Rui, and intercepting countless firearms and supplies transported by the Red bandits to Fujian. The remaining bandits fled in disarray to Donggu, and the armies also surrounded Donggu.

▲ Victory Report from the Headquarters: Donggu, the old nest of the Red bandits, was captured by the right wing army on the 27th after being surrounded. The headquarters staff office has sent a concise telegram of victory. The original telegram stated, "After our army recovered Shicheng and Ningdu, the bandit troops fled back to their old nest in droves, still plotting a final resistance. Our left and right wing army groups took advantage of the situation to converge and attack. According to repeated telegrams from Commander-in-Chief Chen of our right wing Third Route Army, our right wing Third Route Army occupied Shaxi on the 22nd of this month, followed up with a rapid advance, catching the bandits by surprise, and thrusting straight into the bandit's den from behind. On the same day, Commander-in-Chief Cai of our right wing First Army Corps led his troops to attack from the side of Shanggu, breaking through Longgang on the 25th, and then continuing to advance, using lightning tactics to capture the old nest of Donggu in one fell swoop on the 27th. The bandits entrenched in their nests, initially resisting with all their might, but were eventually surrounded by our army, breaking through the key points. The bandits could not take care of each other, so they were completely annihilated without a single one escaping. It is estimated that more than 30,000 large and small bandits were captured, more than 14,200 rifles, and countless other weapons, equipment, documents, rice, and livestock, etc. In addition, comprehensive telegrams from Commander-in-Chief Zhu Shaoliang, Commander-in-Chief Jiang, Commander-in-Chief Sun, Army Commander Chen, Army Commander Zhao, and Army Commander Wei of our left wing army group stated that our Second Route Army advanced from Gulonggang through Yuexi to coordinate the attack on Longgang and Donggu by the left wing army group, and to block the bandits fleeing south. The First Route Army advanced from Qingtangxu north to Yutian Nankengxu, directly attacking Huangpi Xiaobu. The Third Army Corps fiercely attacked Lokoujie Huangpi area from Jinzhu Dongshentou Beijie. The Second Army and Tenth Army of the Fourth Army Corps controlled Shicheng and Ningdu, waiting to intercept and encircle the bandits when they fled outward. After the deployments were completed, the armies began to move on the 23rd, approaching step by step. When entering the nests, the bandits used pre-built fortifications and various firearms, relying on dangerous places, stubbornly resisting our army's fierce attack for several days and nights. Our air force also made every effort to bomb, destroying countless supplies in their nests. The bandits could not withstand it, and our army charged forward bravely, completely recovering Huangpi and Xiaobu on the 25th and 26th. The corpses were piled up everywhere in the bandit nests, and blood stained the mountains and valleys. It is reported that the ringleaders Zhu Mao Huangxiang mostly died in the chaos among the bandits, and no less than 50,000 people were released from coercion and ransom, etc. Donggu, Longgang, Huangpi, and Xiaobu were originally the most important bandit dens and the only major base of the Red bandits in Jiangxi province. All the political and organizational organs of the bandit party were concentrated here. After this sweep, they have been fundamentally annihilated. Special telegram to report the victory. Staff Office of the Nanchang Headquarters, 28th day, 5:35 pm."

Continued News of the Flood in Hubei Province

▲ More Than 50 Counties in the Province Flooded

▲ All Circles Immediately Establish Emergency Relief Association

Hankou Correspondence: This time, the continuous plum rains, rising rivers, and breached dikes have been reported repeatedly. As of yesterday (the 27th), the rain has not stopped, and the disaster area in the province has reached more than 50 counties. The streets of Wuhan have also been flooded, truly a rare disaster unseen in decades. The situation is recorded as follows:

▲ Disaster Situation in Various Counties: The counties have long suffered from bandit troubles, and the people have been displaced. After the active suppression of bandits by various armies, the situation has gradually been cleared. The government then tried to summon the refugees to engage in farming, in order to gradually restore the vitality of the countryside. After sowing, the rainfall was quite even, and it was generally expected to be a good year. Unexpectedly, as the rice and wheat were about to ripen, continuous rain fell, and much of the grain rotted. In addition, the water was raging, breaching dikes and dams, and submerging fields and houses. The number of people who died in the water is countless. For example, in the Yangtze River basin, the counties of Badong, Zigui, Xingshan, Changyang, Yichang, Yidu, Dangyang, Zhijiang, Songzi, Jiangling, Jianli, Shishou, Mianyang, Jiayu, Hanyang, Wuchang, Huanggang, Qishui, Qichun, Daye, Yangxin, Guangji, and Huangmei, and in the Xiang River basin, the counties of Yicheng, Zhongxiang, Qianjiang, and Hanchuan, and along the Zhang and Yun rivers, the counties of Yingshan, Anlu, Yunmeng, and Xiaogan have all suffered unprecedented disasters. The county magistrates of various counties sent telegrams to the province, requesting relief more than ten times a day.

▲ Wuhan Flood Situation: Wuhan is the place where the Yangtze and Han rivers converge. Half a month ago, the Xiang River rose, almost level with the banks. Afterwards, it continued to rise. The water of the Yangtze River also increased day by day. The low-lying areas of the inner streets of Hankou, due to excessive accumulation of water that could not be discharged, had long been submerged and navigable by boats. On the 27th, the river water suddenly rose by more than ten feet, overflowing the banks. The most prosperous areas, such as Jianghanguan, Xinsheng Road, Zhongshan Road, Jiaotong Road, the Post Office, Special District One, Special District Two, Special District Three, and the French and Japanese concessions, were all flooded, and traffic was cut off. In Wuchang, Hanyangmen, Kuaizijie, Pinghumen, Qingshiqiao, Juwanjie, Gongyuanjie, etc., were also flooded. In Hanyang, due to the long-term ban on ferries, it was not possible to investigate, but it was roughly estimated that more than half of the area was also flooded. The Wuhan market was greatly affected by the flood, and the prices of all goods soared, even vegetables had doubled in price.

▲ Strict Dike Protection: As the flood spread, the Zhanggong Dike, which protects Hankou, and the Wutai and Wufeng sluices, which protect Wuchang, were all closely watched. The provincial government, the Department of Civil Affairs, the Department of Construction, the Hankou Municipal Government, the Water Conservancy Bureau, the Provincial Public Security Bureau, the Water Police Bureau, and the Garrison Headquarters all sent personnel to recruit workers, investigate, and provide emergency protection, and were extremely busy. Chen Keming, director of the Water Conservancy Bureau, personally inspected the dikes and sluices. The Garrison Department also sent teams to guard them. According to the survey, although cracks were found in the Zhanggong Dike, they were straight lines and did not pose any danger. The Wutai Sluice was also safe, but the Wufeng Sluice was quite dangerous due to damage to the gate panels. In addition, on the 25th, the Garrison Department captured seven Red bandits digging the dike at Zhanggong Dike. It was reported that 23 others were at large. Soldiers have now been added to defend, and there should be no accidents. As for temporary flood control, the representatives of various agencies and groups held a meeting and decided to set up temporary flood control offices in Wuchang, Hankou, and Hanyang. The Wuchang office was attached to the Water Conservancy Bureau, the Hankou office was attached to the Municipal Government, and the Hanyang office was attached to the County Government. A hundred earthen dikes were built, and water was pumped out to restore traffic in Wuhan as soon as possible.

▲ Preparing for Relief: For the sake of providing relief to the disaster victims, the provincial government specifically decided at the political meeting on the 20th to telegraph the Central Relief Committee to allocate large sums of money, and to telegraph various provinces to raise relief funds to provide relief. At the same time, the provincial government and the Department of Civil Affairs sent personnel to the disaster areas to investigate quickly. On the 23rd, another meeting was held to decide to entrust the Water Conservancy Bureau to preside over the repair of the Wuhan dikes and the construction of the Department of Construction, the Provincial Public Security Bureau, the Hankou Municipal Government, the Hankou Public Security Bureau, and other agencies to assist. In addition, the rice stored in the Ping Tiao Bureau was not sold by auction, but reserved for relief to the counties. The existing rice has been distributed, first to Yunmeng and other eight counties, and other counties will be dealt with separately. However, the flood has been increasing in recent days, and the situation is even more urgent. The provincial government then held a meeting on the 27th and decided to establish a Flood Emergency Relief Committee, extensively inviting celebrities from all circles of the party, government, military, and business to jointly seek relief.

▲ Relief Association Established: The chairman of the provincial government, He Chengjun, convened a meeting of all circles of the party, government, and military at the Hankou General Chamber of Commerce at 3:00 p.m. on the 28th to discuss relief measures. Those present included Garrison Commander Xia Douyin, Civil Affairs Director Liu Wendao, Finance Director Wu Guozhen, Construction Director Fang Dazhi, Peng Jieshi of the Provincial Committee, Ma Dengying, Zhu Huaibing, Zuo Duo, Liu Yun, Wen Juntian of the Municipal Committee, Mayor He Baohua, Chamber of Commerce Chairman He Hengfu, and more than 100 bank presidents. Chairman He Chengjun reported on the flood situation. Then Liu Wendao spoke, saying that fundraising was too slow and that a loan of 300,000 yuan should first be obtained from the banking group, with the government responsible for repayment. After discussion of various proposals, it was decided (1) to establish the Flood Emergency Relief Committee immediately. Those present at the meeting today are natural members of the committee. The location of the committee is attached to the General Chamber of Commerce, and in accordance with the organizational charter, He Chengjun, Ma Dengying, Zhu Huaibing, Zuo Duo, Wen Juntian, He Hengfu, Chen Jingyu, Su Taiyu, Yue Huanting, Cai Fuqing, and Yu Chongwei were elected as standing committee members. (2) Chen Keming, director of the Water Conservancy Bureau, was to go to various counties to inspect the dike projects, and the entire staff of the Water Conservancy Bureau and the Department of Construction would participate in the Wuhan protection work, under the command of Fang Dazhi and Peng Jieshi. (3) The engineer corps of all divisions and brigades stationed in Wuhan were to participate in the emergency rescue work. If necessary, infantry could be dispatched. (4) Fang Dazhi and Peng Jieshi were to go to various dikes to investigate and plan, and the public security chiefs of the two provinces of Wuhan and Hankou were also to strictly supervise their subordinates to investigate and report any breaches. After the meeting, He convened the first meeting of the Standing Committee, passed the organizational charter, and announced its establishment, and elected He Chengjun as chairman, Ma Dengying as director of the General Affairs Section, Zhu Huaibing as deputy, He Hengfu as director of the Fundraising Section, Su Taiyu as deputy, Cai Fuqing as director of the Relief Section, Chen Jingyu as deputy, Yu Chongwei as director of the Audit Section, Yue Shouting as deputy, Zuo Duo as director of the Investigation Section, and Wen Juntian as deputy. From this day on, they would come to the meeting to work in order to actively provide relief to the disaster victims. (July 28th)

The Flood in Southern Anhui is Extremely Severe

▲ Rice-Snatching Riots Occur in Various Places

▲ Chen Tiaoyuan Arrives in Wuhu from Liu'an

▲ Ban Rice Exports to Maintain People's Food Supply

Wuhu Correspondence: Among the provinces along the Yangtze River, Anhui Province is the most severely affected by the flood. More than 40 counties in the province have been submerged. Southern Anhui relies heavily on agricultural products. At this time when the autumn harvest is approaching, the losses from this flood are incalculable. All counties such as Xuancheng, Nanling, Fanchang, Wuwei, and Tongcheng have been almost completely submerged. The two major weirs of Fenghuang and Linmapu in Wuhu and the Huangsitan weir in Wuwei have all collapsed one after another. Today, the Baoda weir in Fanchang has also been affected. In total, more than three or four million mu of fertile land in the counties of southern Anhui have been submerged, forming a vast expanse of water for hundreds of miles around. A few days ago, a rice merchant from Tongcheng loaded 1,100 shi of rice and came to Wuhu. When passing through Gaokengpu, 20 li away from Wuhu, it was robbed by the disaster victims. Last night, a wheat boat arrived at Pangxiexi and was looted by hundreds of refugees nearby. Six of the boat crew and owners were beaten, and one elderly man was in critical condition. All have been taken to Zhong Shouzhis Hospital on Zhongshan Road for treatment. Rice-snatching incidents in other towns and villages are occurring frequently every day. People are restless, and unruly elements are taking the opportunity to incite them. The situation is extremely worrying. Dozens of bandits arrived at Lugang Town, 15 li away from Wuhu, last night, joining hundreds of disaster victims to loot many shops in the town and attempt to seize the firearms of the defense corps. Fortunately, the defense was tight and they were unable to succeed. However, the bandit ships have not gone far, and the situation is very tense. This morning, the head of the defense corps, She Hongqian, and others came to Wuhu to request troops. Wang Leshan, the brigade commander of the 171st Brigade, sent a company of soldiers to attack by small steamer. This morning, the leaders of all circles of the party, government, military, police, gentry, and business in Wuhu held a joint meeting at the county government to discuss emergency relief measures for the flood. It was decided to organize a flood relief association. In addition to asking the provincial government and fellow Anhui natives abroad, such as Xu Shiying, for donations, they would first borrow 3,000 yuan from the Bank of China in Wuhu, together with 1,000 yuan raised on the spot, to be used for emergency relief and to stabilize rice prices, which should not exceed 11 yuan per shi. Public sales offices were set up, and temples and schools in higher-lying areas were selected to establish refugee shelters. It is estimated that in Wuhu city alone, more than 800 households had their houses flooded. Disaster victims from other villages and towns came to the city seeking food everywhere. After the meeting, Chen Tiaoyuan, the chairman of the Anhui provincial government, happened to return to Wuhu from Liu'an after suppressing bandits, and everyone went to the Jianggan to wait for him. Chen took the Rongchang steamer via Hefei and arrived at the port at 5:00 p.m. After landing, he went to the third floor of the Zhonghua Hotel to meet with people from all walks of life. Chen said that the bandits in Liu'an had been severely hit and were not a threat for the time being. The emergency relief was extremely important because the flood in various counties of this province was so severe. Therefore, he had to return to Anqing first to prepare for emergency relief. Once the relief was somewhat effective, he planned to go to Nanchang immediately to discuss with Chairman Chiang the thorough strategy for bandit suppression. As for the widespread flood damage this time, which covered the entire Anhui province, Hefei was more than ten feet under water, and Wuhu and the counties in southern Anhui, which were the rice-producing areas of this province, had suffered such heavy damage, and in the future there was a danger of hardship from top to bottom. The only thing to do in the near future was to first allocate several thousand yuan for emergency relief, and for the sake of the people's food supply throughout the province, to immediately ban the export of rice and grain, and then to organize a flood relief organization in the province. Then he went to the residence of Yang Chunpu, the former director of the rice donation bureau, for dinner. At 9:00 p.m., he changed to a small Wuhu steamer and returned to Anqing directly. That evening, all circles in Wuhu also telegraphed the province, requesting a clear order to prohibit the export of rice and grain, the telegram stating, "Chen Junjian, Chairman of the Anhui Provincial Government, continuous rain in recent days has caused flooding, and the weirs and fields have been completely submerged. The same is true for all counties in Anhui Province. Rice prices are soaring and cannot be suppressed. If we do not think of the future and prevent it, and ban the export of rice from the province, the starving people of Anhui Province will inevitably become starving corpses. In addition to organizing a flood relief association to maintain the current situation, a meeting was held and it was decided to telegraph immediately for a clear order to ban the export of rice from the province in order to save the disaster victims and maintain the people's food supply. Sincerely, the Wuhu County Consolidation Committee, County Government, Public Security Bureau, County Chamber of Commerce, and County Education Bureau." (July 28th)

The Flood Disaster in Henan Province is Severe

▲ Heavy Rain in Shangcai for Several Weeks

▲ Rivers in Wuyang Collapse and Break

Kaifeng Correspondence: The flood situation in various counties of Henan Province is also extremely serious. The reports from Shangcai and Wuyang counties are recorded as follows: Li Yuan, the magistrate of Shangcai County, reported that the county had been continuously overcast and rainy, without stopping for several weeks, and there had been torrential rain for three days and nights. The area near the city was higher in elevation, but the accumulated water was also three feet deep. In places with lower elevation, such as Huangbu, Xiaogan, Xindi, Chenzhai, Rufen, Zengfu, Yangqiu, Kangning, and Wangli, the land for dozens of li in all directions had become a marshland. Countless fields and houses were washed away, and many people and livestock were drowned. The cries of sorrow were heard everywhere, too terrible to bear. In addition to conducting a detailed investigation of the disaster in each district and reporting it in another case, he was requesting an emergency relief to save the disaster victims. In addition, Xu Futian, the magistrate of Wuyang County, reported in a telegram on behalf of the county that since the beginning of June, there had been continuous rain for several weeks, mountain floods had broken out, and the Li River, Ni River, Sha River, and Hui River within the territory had successively breached their banks by tens or hundreds of zhang. The villages and fields along the rivers had all become marshlands. The areas most severely affected were Qili Township and Duanzhuang Township in the first district, Tianzhuang Township and Qiaozhang Township in the second district, Dihu Township in the sixth district, and the banks of the Sha and Hui Rivers in the seventh district. It was estimated that thousands of houses had been washed away and countless livestock drowned. The autumn crops that had been planted were completely submerged. Cries of sorrow were heard everywhere, too terrible to bear. Farming was hopeless, and the lives of the people were in danger. The disaster was serious, an unprecedented flood in 20 years, and they were requesting an emergency relief to provide aid. The Provincial Relief Association has sent personnel with money to distribute it and has also forwarded the situation to the National Relief Association and various charitable organizations in the north and south.

Mr. Wang Rongbao's Speech Upon Arrival in Shenyang

Shenyang Dispatch: Mr. Wang Rongbao, the resident ambassador to Japan, was dispatched by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to Korea to investigate the massacre. Having completed his mission and returned to the country, he arrived in Andong on the 23rd. At 8:45 PM that evening, he boarded the Anfeng train to Shenyang, arriving in Liaoning at 6:20 AM on the 24th. Those who welcomed him at the station included Mr. Li Ruzhou, Deputy Adjutant-General of the Border Defense Command, representing Deputy Commander Zhang; Mr. Sun, an adjutant representing Zhang Zuoxiang; Mr. Wang Jinghuan, Special Diplomatic Commissioner representing Zang Shiyi, Chairman of the Liaoning Provincial Government; and over forty Chinese and Japanese news reporters. He alighted at the Kaining Hotel on Yangsan Jinglu Road. Reporters met him in the train, where Mr. Wang shared the investigation process.

Following his assignment to investigate the case, he departed from Tokyo with the consul on the 13th. He arrived in Busan on the 15th, Seoul on the 16th, and Pyongyang on the 17th. After staying for two days, he went to Chinampo, then returned to Seoul, followed by Incheon, and then back to Seoul before arriving in Sinuiju. The investigation journey lasted a total of twelve days. The investigation revealed that the damage in Pyongyang was the most severe. Based on confirmed reports, ninety-five Chinese compatriots were killed, and over two hundred were injured. The whereabouts of others remain unknown. The loss of property has not been accurately calculated, but the Chamber of Commerce estimates it to be over two million. Next was Incheon, with two deaths and losses of less than one hundred thousand. There were two deaths each in Wonsan and Sinuiju. Chinampo and Seoul did not suffer significant damage. The riot in Pyongyang occurred on the 5th, a Sunday. The Japanese side received the news that evening but thought it was not serious. In reality, the Korean people were highly organized in their plans for the riot, and the situation suddenly escalated uncontrollably. The Japanese police were scattered in various locations, and it took time to gather them. By the time the Japanese police mobilized and came out to suppress the riot, our compatriots had already suffered significant casualties and damages. In Sinuiju, due to its proximity to our border in Andong, there was close communication regarding defense, and the incident was immediately suppressed. This was largely due to the efforts of our officials and police. Personally, I feel that this tragic incident is extremely serious and cannot be resolved through simple negotiations. Observing this incident, the Wanbaoshan incident was very small, and logically it was insufficient to cause such a major event. It was ultimately caused by three factors: (1) Misreporting by Japanese and Korean news reporters; (2) Ignorant Koreans being misled; (3) Ineffective prevention by the Japanese police. My personal view on this case can be summarized in two sentences: Compensation for damage, no compensation for no damage. Given the severity of the damage, Japan should be responsible for compensation. Japanese government's attitude: Shidehara [Kijuro] expressed to me that he felt deeply saddened by this tragic incident under the current global situation and under Japanese territory. He felt obligated to provide condolences and relief, but there was much debate on the issue of international legal responsibility. Therefore, the Japanese government absolutely refuses to admit the point of compensation. Accepting international legal responsibility may cause the current cabinet to be overthrown by the Japanese people. Our country has insisted on compensation. If a satisfactory resolution cannot be reached, the only final option is for all Chinese compatriots in Korea to return home. I plan to stay in Shenyang for one or two days to investigate the truth of the Wanbaoshan incident and then go to [Heilongjiang] to meet Deputy Commander Zhang to seek his instructions. Then, I will go to the capital to report to the National Government and discuss negotiation methods. The location may be in Tokyo or Nanjing. I personally prefer Nanjing. I do not plan to stay long in the capital and will return to my post. The reporter asked about Japan's diplomacy toward China. Wang Rongbao replied that Shidehara had solemnly stated to him that he would not change his policy, no matter what attacks he received from political parties. Japan is willing to negotiate the Sino-Japanese jurisdictional issue on conditions, and it is not true that they are unwilling to negotiate immediately. On the railway issue, Japan also does not insist on the parallel line issue, ultimately aiming for coexistence and co-prosperity. With the existing railways in the Northeast and the South Manchuria Railway, Director Kimura will come to Liaoning after finishing his affairs in Tokyo and will definitely start negotiations. He will not delay. Japan will never give up its vested interests in Manchuria and Mongolia under any cabinet. However, he has faced many difficulties in years of diplomatic negotiation and has never had a day of peace. (July 24th)

All Sectors in Jinan Establish an Anti-Japanese Association

Jinan Dispatch: All sectors in Jinan are deeply angered by the Wanbaoshan Incident and the massacre of overseas Chinese by Koreans. Consequently, various trade associations have initiated the organization of an Anti-Japanese Overseas Chinese Protection Association. On the 26th, at 2:00 PM, they invited various trade associations and farmers' associations to hold a meeting at the auditorium of the county party headquarters to discuss methods of action. Over sixty representatives from various trade associations and farmers' associations attended, along with Fang Ziying and others representing the county party headquarters. Fang Ziying reported on the progress of the Korean case and the public's anger. Next, they discussed methods of action and resolved to (1) establish a preparatory office for the Jinan Anti-Japanese Overseas Chinese Protection Association, and nominated Feng Zhensheng (Guangdong goods), Wang Bozhou (newspapers), Li Mengfu (transport), Zhang Guansan (cotton), Fu Yuting (cigarettes), Cui Zihong (shoes and hats), Du Zhensheng (wood), Zhang Pinzhi (general merchandise), Tian Zhongtao (alcohol), Ma Yichen (fresh goods), Zhang Yufu (silk and cloth), Zhang Jiyuan (salt), Guo Zuoting (flour), Qiao Xiaozhou (farmers' association), Zhang Yanchen (pharmaceuticals), and fifteen others to be responsible for preparation and action. (2) On August 2nd, a formal establishment conference will be convened for various agencies, groups, and schools in the county and city to elect executive and supervisory committee members. The meeting adjourned at around 4:00 PM, and the atmosphere was extremely tense throughout the entire event. (July 26th)

Shandong Province Preserves the Chen Family's Ancient Seals

▲The Library is Negotiating Purchase

Jinan Dispatch: In Shandong's Weixian County, the Chen, Cao, Guo, and Gao families are the most famous for collecting antiquities. However, their descendants have declined in recent times, and they have begun to sell the antiquities. The Qin and Han bricks and tiles of the Gao family are only a small part. The most famous collection belongs to Chen Fuzhai. After Chen's death, everything was equally divided among his three sons, including one share for the Mao Gong Ding and four-eared *dun* bronze vessel (it has long been rumored that the Mao Gong Ding was sold to the Japanese, but it is actually treasured by Zhou Shutao and kept secret from others; even rubbings are sold for one hundred and sixty yuan, and a Westerner once estimated the ding's value at five million yuan, which shows how precious it is. The four-eared *dun* bronze vessel was indeed bought by the Japanese), one share for the ten *zhong* bells (although the Chen family called it "ten bells," there were actually eleven bells. When it was sold to the Japanese, only nine were given, and a fake one was added to make up ten, while two were hidden. Later, the Japanese found out and offered a high price to buy them, and eventually all of them went to Japan), and one share for the ten thousand seals. In addition, there were over ten thousand ancient pottery shards and two bronze mirrors, which were also divided equally. So far, the *ding*, *dun*, and ten *zhong* bells have all been sold. Only the ten thousand seals remain. Chen's collection of seals is documented in the *Wan Yin Lou Seal Catalog*, which is the most comprehensive. Each volume of the catalog sells for six hundred yuan, and even photocopies sell for sixteen yuan. It is said that although the collection is called "ten thousand seals," in addition to those falsely attributed to others, there are actually over six thousand two hundred pieces "some say over six thousand five hundred." Recently, after Gao Hansheng sold the Qin and Han bricks and tiles from his Shangtao Studio to the Japanese, the Chen family also considered selling the seals. It is said that three Japanese people lingered in Tanxian, negotiating a purchase and offering one hundred and twenty thousand yuan. However, the local authorities found out and expelled the Japanese. Therefore, the Chen family indirectly expressed a willingness to sell to the provincial library, taking less than the Japanese price, to show respect for the government's intention to preserve antiquities. They are currently in negotiations. As for the pottery shards, ancient mirrors, and ancient bricks, they are also being sold to the library. The value of complete pottery shards with inscriptions is fifty cents each, and broken ones are half that price. The price of the ancient mirrors has not yet been negotiated. It is said that the Chen family's bronze mirrors have all types and are all polished on one side and have flowers and inscriptions on the other. Two of the mirrors, when the floral side is shone in sunlight, the flowers can pass through the mirror and be projected onto the wall, like a modern movie; they are truly treasures. Unfortunately, one is broken, and only one remains. Also, for the over one thousand ancient bricks and tiles, it was agreed that those identical to the Gao family's Qin and Han bricks and tiles purchased by the library would not be accepted, and the remaining ones would be fairly priced. At the same time, the Cao (Hongxun) family's collection of over one thousand ancient bricks and the Guo family's collection of over three thousand ancient seals in Weixian County are also being negotiated for sale to the library, and they have all expressed a willingness to accept a low price, but the government needs to raise tens of thousands of yuan to purchase everything. The current library director, Wang Xiantang, plans to suggest to the library design committee that they quickly determine fundraising methods to purchase all the above antiquities and the books from the Haiyuan Pavilion to preserve them.

152nd Regular Meeting of the Central Committee

▲Special Commissioner to Xinjiang Province Recalled and Reassigned

▲People's Organizations Must Be Reorganized or Organized by a Deadline

The 152nd meeting of the Central Executive Committee of the Kuomintang was held at 8:00 AM on July 30th in the first conference hall of the Central Party Headquarters.
