Progress of the Capital Antiquities Institute's Exhibition

Since Shu Chushi took over the Nanjing Antiquities Preservation Institute, he has made great efforts to rectify it, employing workers to repair the buildings and grounds, giving them a new look. He has collected bells, tripods, *yi* vessels, bricks, tiles, steles, and stone inscriptions, as well as famous calligraphy and paintings, selecting the best for display to facilitate research. Archaeology can correct historical omissions and promote social interest in academic research, which is of great importance to cultural progress. Currently, they are compiling a catalog of antiquities from various dynasties, making systematic records to ensure that visitors have a clear understanding of historical events. They are now striving to expand further to meet public expectations. Last month, they specifically requested the Ministry of Education to jointly issue an official letter to all provinces and cities across the country, instructing their subordinates to widely collect and send to the institute historical and cultural relics, calligraphy and paintings, stele rubbings, stone relics, and photographs of famous sites in their respective regions for public viewing. It is expected that after this solicitation, the exhibits at the institute will be even richer.

Bandit Leader Widow Zhang Executed in Western Henan

Luoyang Dispatch: The 65th Division of the National Army recently suppressed bandits in western Henan and captured the notorious bandit leader Widow Zhang. After interrogation, she was executed by firing squad on July 22nd. The following is a record of her confession: Zhang Bingqing, alias Yu Jie, was captured by the 65th Division in the seventh district of Pingdeng County and sent to the Luoyang Western Workers' Supervision Office for interrogation. Official (Q): Where are you from? How old are you? Where is your maiden home? Where is your husband's home? (A): Luoning, 46 years old, maiden home is Qiangtou in Luoning, husband's home is Beicun in Luoning. (Q): How many people are in your family? How much land do you cultivate? (A): My parents-in-law, my husband, four brothers, my three nephews, and three daughters-in-law. We have five or six hundred mu of land. (Q): What are the names of your father-in-law, your mother-in-law's surname, and the names of your husband and sons? (A): Father-in-law Zhang Luoshan, mother-in-law Wang, husband Zhang Shudou, eldest son Zhang Mingsheng, second son Zhang Zhensheng, third son Zhang Guangsheng. (Q): Why did you go out and become a bandit leader? (A): My maiden name is He. I married at fourteen. My husband died early, leaving behind three sons. My father-in-law was killed by bandits, and my mother-in-law died from opium addiction. Later, the property was divided. My eldest son died of illness. My second son used to be a company commander, but later he came home, and I did not ask him to go out and do anything. My third son was studying at home. Unexpectedly, my husband's fourth younger brother, Shukui, killed my two sons and sold all three of my daughters-in-law. Because my entire family died, I became angry and sold a lot of land to buy hundreds of guns to become a bandit leader. (Q): Why did your husband's fourth younger brother, Shukui, collude with bandits to kill your sons? (A): My husband had four brothers. After the family was divided, the fourth younger brother did not engage in proper business, smoked opium, and did not do good things. He squandered the family property and intended to kill my entire family to plot for my share of the family property. It is now heard that the fourth brother has fled abroad, and his whereabouts are unknown. (Q): Where were you when your sons were killed by your fourth younger brother? (A): I happened to be visiting my maiden home and was fortunate to escape unharmed. (Q): How much family property do you still have, and who manages it? (A): There are still a hundred mu of bamboo land at home. It is now heard that it is managed by my clansman Yongquan. (Q): Explain in detail what you have been through since you became a bandit leader these past few years. (A): I have been living in the team for these past few years and have never returned home. I paid for many of the guns for the various bandit groups. Most of the bandit groups listened to my orders. People like Li and Zhang are all my adopted sons. When I attacked Luoning City last year, I allocated a battalion of guns and soldiers to Wang Laowu. In May and June of this year, I gathered various bandit groups in the Longmen area to form some teams, preparing to surrender. (Q): How many bandit groups did you gather in the end? Who were the bandit leaders? How many guns and soldiers were there in total? (A): In Longmen, I discussed with many bandit leaders such as Yang Delian, Han Qiulin, Li Zuoxin, Li Qifang, Wen Zhi, Du Keqin, Guo Jiulao, Wu Mingli, Dong Faru, and Zhang Tianwei. It was estimated that we could gather ten thousand people. Li Shichen also arrived and added eight bandit groups. We wanted to gather all the teams and form three divisions. We had gathered over three thousand people, but the organization had not yet been completed. There were three thousand rifles, and the rest were submachine guns, as well as four machine guns. Just as we were discussing, the army arrived at various passes to intercept us, scattering my teams. Many bandit leaders fled and were captured. Now that my revenge has been taken, I have no regrets about dying. It is only my dissatisfaction that they will get all the land in my family for nothing.

Local Dispatches

Songjiang

The 4th Battalion of the Tax Police Returns for Training: After the Special Task Force of the Tax Police of the Ministry of Finance was dispatched to Bengbu last month, lasting two months, only the 4th company of the Independent 4th Battalion remained stationed at the gunpowder depot. Recently, Chief Wang ordered the 4th Battalion to return to this county for training. Battalion Commander Jia Youhui, following orders, led his troops to Songjiang on the afternoon of the 28th.

County Government Meeting Minutes: The County Government held its 118th County Government Meeting yesterday (29th), chaired by County Magistrate Shen. Discussions included (1) A petition from the County Chamber of Commerce to restrict private rickshaws, proposing to limit the number of private rickshaws to three-tenths of the number of commercial rickshaws. Resolved: The County Government will submit a request to the Construction Department for approval. (2) The County Government building requires an estimated cost of over 3,000 yuan for repairs. Discussion on how to raise these funds. Resolved: The local finances are extremely depleted, with no way to raise funds. The County Government will submit a request to the Provincial Department for funding.

Suzhou

Someone Falls to Their Death on Jinmen City Wall: At around 9:00 PM on the 29th, a person wearing short clothes, about thirty years old, fell from the Jinmen City Wall in Suzhou, suffering serious injuries to the head and abdomen, and died immediately. The jurisdictional police district reported to the local prosecutor's office, which dispatched personnel on the afternoon of the 30th to conduct an on-site examination. Several injuries were found during the examination, indicating that the person had been beaten before death. Since no family members were present, the local security guard prepared a coffin for burial. Officials suspect that the person was beaten on the city wall before being pushed down, and are investigating the perpetrators. Two suspects were arrested that night, but there were no conclusive confessions.

Merchants Hold Meeting on Economic Disengagement from Japan: The Merchant Group's Meeting on Economic Disengagement from Japan, organized by the County Chamber of Commerce, held its first meeting on the 30th, chaired by Shi Junqing. Resolutions included (1) Dividing into seven sections: General Affairs, Economics, Documents, Investigation, Registration, Research, and Publicity. (2) The issue of Japanese yarn as raw material for the cloth factory association was handed over to the research section for research. (3) Raising 1,000 yuan for overseas Chinese relief funds. (4) Appointed Xu Xiaozhai and eight others as standing committee members, assigning duties to each section.

Divorce Appeal Case to be Announced Today: Zheng Shaopo, the manager of the Norway National Shipping Company, was sued by his wife, Zheng Su Xuewu, in the Shanghai District Court for taking concubines and causing injury, seeking a divorce and requesting 10,000 yuan in alimony. The Shanghai Court ruled that Zheng Shaopo would be fined 20 yuan for the injury, while the other claims were not accepted. Zheng Su Xuewu, dissatisfied with the ruling, hired lawyer Lu Hongyi to appeal to the High Court. A meeting was held on the 30th to hear the case, with both the plaintiff and defendant summoned to court. The judge advised reconciliation, but the two sides had conflicting opinions, and reconciliation failed. The debate then began. The judge announced the end of the debate and scheduled the verdict for the 31st (today).

Chuansha

County Magistrate Accused and Ordered to Transfer to the Province: County Magistrate Tu Guangjun, due to falsely accusing the party as communist, undermining education, and illegally detaining County Supervisor Song Chengjun, has aroused public outrage in the area. Petitions were filed with the provincial government requesting investigation and removal. The provincial government commissioned Chen Bingbo, Yi Zuolin, and others to come to Chuansha to investigate. Now, the provincial government has ordered County Magistrate Tu Guangjun to transfer to the province. The vacancy will be filled by the current Magistrate of Jingjiang County, Li Leng. After receiving the order, Magistrate Tu has completed the county affairs and left Chuansha on the morning of the 29th. All handover procedures are delegated to Secretary Hu Yirong. The new county magistrate is scheduled to take office on August 1st.

Changshu

Sandbank Dams Cut Off Sanzhangpu River: This continuous rain has caused disasters, with low-lying areas being flooded. Even the high-lying areas in the west are affected. The waterway in the west, Sanzhangpu River, relies entirely on accepting water from the eastern lakes and connecting to the three branches of Shazhou to the west, discharging into the Yangtze River. Irrigation and water conservancy are regulated in this manner. Unexpectedly, recently, some residents of Shazhou, due to the rising water level in Shazhou, built dams to block the southern end of the three branches of Shazhou (i.e., the downstream of Sanzhangpu River) on the 26th, preventing the water from Sanzhangpu River from being discharged, threatening to flood tens of thousands of mu of land on both sides of Sanzhangpu River. Not satisfied, the residents of Shazhou blocked the southern end of the second branch. District Chief Shen Changjun was unable to stop them and telegraphed the county government for instructions on the 28th. After receiving the telegram, the county government considered the great importance of this action to the water conservancy of the interior and the potential for disputes. The county government immediately ordered the Public Security Bureau to instruct the Shazhou Public Security Sub-bureau to rush to the scene, demolish the dams that had been built, stop those who were building, and prohibit construction.

Yuanhua Township Again Suffers Robbery: Qin Jilun, a resident of Hebo Township in Yuanhua District in the southern part of the county, had considerable savings. Unexpectedly, at around 10:00 PM on the 26th, bandit boats arrived and landed in the area. They first went to the home of Qin Guanguan (Jilun's nephew). In a moment of desperation, Guanguan said, "I am a poor man. My uncle is rich, you can go there." The bandits followed him and arrived at the back door of Qin Jilun's home. Guanguan took the opportunity to escape. The bandits began to knock on the door. Jilun knew something was wrong and escaped from the roof. His wife, Huang, was dragged out of bed by the bandits and forced to reveal the location of the hidden money. When Huang refused to answer, the bandits beat her severely with sticks. Her son, Shisheng, was also beaten. As a result, they were robbed of over ninety yuan in cash, two gold rings, one gold bracelet, and clothing, etc. The trousseau that Huang had prepared for her daughter's upcoming wedding was also destroyed by the bandits. Afterwards, Jilun sent the injured Huang by boat to the Jisheng Hospital in the city for treatment. It is reported that her life is not in danger.

Notorious Bandit Zheng Yushan's Son Seeks Revenge for His Father: The town of Xiyang in Fushan is garrisoned by an anti-smuggling brigade to guard the sea entrance. Ever since the sea bandit leader Zheng Yushan was executed

, his son Zheng Ming has been constantly leading his gang to harass various towns in an attempt to retaliate. His踪跡 often have been found in Xiyang, Wangshi, and other towns. The troops stationed there have been closely guarding against him. At around 9:00 PM on the night before last (27th), the anti-smuggling team stationed in the town, led by Captain Zhang Xiuwen, patrolled the coast. Only two unarmed team members were left to guard the team post. Unexpectedly, at around 10:00 PM, over thirty pirates arrived by two sea-sand boats, landed with weapons, and surrounded the anti-smuggling post. Both guards were tied up and forced to reveal the location of the weapons. The guards replied that the team had taken them on patrol. The pirates had no choice but to leave, but the next morning, the pirates went to Xiyang again, intending to seize weapons from the anti-smuggling unit in the same way. Fortunately, the unit was alerted by the guards and was prepared, so it was not robbed. The pirates left angrily, but before leaving, the gang shouted, "We will not rest until we capture and execute Liu Zhiyi of the water police team who arrested Zheng Yushan!" Therefore, the unit has tightened security and also telegraphed its superiors, requesting additional troops to come to Changshu for defense.

Jiangyin

Organizing a Committee for Economic Severance with Japan: The county chamber of commerce held a members' meeting on the afternoon of the 27th. Ninety-six members attended. Wu Shuying presided. (1) Passed the budget statement for the 20th year. (2) Sent a telegram to the Yuan and Ministry, strongly protesting and striving for justice in the Wanbaoshan Incident, raising funds to aid overseas Chinese, and organizing a Committee for Economic Severance with Japan, with the executive and supervisory committee members of the chamber of commerce and the chairmen of various trade associations as members. Another meeting will be held later to establish the committee. (3) Police donations from various industries are unaffordable. A letter will be sent to the Public Security Bureau for investigation and cancellation. Other matters were omitted.

The Second Day of the County Representatives' Congress: The third session of the county representatives' congress was held on the morning of the second day to discuss proposals. The most important of these was the proposal by the county farmers' association regarding flood relief, and the proposal by Feng Jiaxi and others to establish a Jiangyin Flood Relief Committee to provide relief to various flood-stricken villages. It was decided that the county reorganization committee should, together with the county government, convene various institutions and organizations to quickly establish a flood relief committee. In the afternoon, candidates for the county executive and supervisory committees were elected. The county was allocated five executive committee members, three alternates, three supervisory committee members, and one alternate. After double the number were selected, they were submitted to the province for approval. Provincial committee member Chen Kanghe served as the supervisor of the election. The results of the vote were: Liu Youkang, Wu Fengnian, Yu Weiqing, Ren Shengxiang, Xu Zukun, Xi Hanping, Gu Di, Wang Yanbin, Ren Hongxin, Xu Er'ying, Tang Kesheng, Zhang Erjie, Huang Bingying, Yang Lupu, Lu Guanzhang, and Jiang Liquan were elected as candidates for the executive committee. Xue Chan, Wang Jihua, Chen Jingchen, Wang Bingchu, Yin Quan, Zhou Zhonghui, Wu Baotong, and Cai Peifu were elected as candidates for the supervisory committee. Around 5:00 PM, the election for provincial representatives was held again. Forty-two representatives attended. The results of the vote were: Liu Youkang, Xi Hanping, Tang Kesheng, Xue Chan, and Cai Peifu were elected.

Nantong

Wounded Soldiers' Vocational Training Factory Opens: Wounded soldiers from the 11th Division of the Army, continuously arrived in Tong from Jinghan [Beijing-Hankou Railway]. The vocational training factory was established by borrowing the poor people's factory, and is now ready and has begun operation. The towels, cotton cloth, socks, and other items produced are all for military use. The wounded soldiers still receive their original monthly pay.

Bandits in Huai Narrowly Avoid Capture: Bandit leaders Ding Chengshun, Ge Ruiting, and Zhang Wenzhong, due to strict pursuit, fled to Qingjiangpu, where they were apprehended by the police. He Xian, the magistrate of Huaiyin, telegraphed the county government on the 29th, requesting that police be sent to escort them back.

Fierce Police-Bandit Battle in Xuejiayuan: In the Xuejiayuan area north of Jiuhua Mountain, a large group of armed bandits suddenly arrived around midnight on the 28th. After being intercepted by the garrison police, the bandits resisted stubbornly. The bandits only scattered and fled at dawn.

Wuxi

Robbery and Murder Case in Jiejingxu: The Shi Fuji family in Shijia Village, Jiejing, in the 5th district of the county (Tianshang City), recently had their fields flooded and the embankment collapsed. They were raising cash to find a way to remedy the situation. Unexpectedly, after 11:00 PM the night before last, the whole family was asleep when they suddenly heard many people banging wildly on the door. Shi suspected that neighbors were calling to protect the embankment, so he rushed to open the door and go outside. However, a dozen bandits rushed inside. One bandit pointed a gun at Shi Fuji, aiming to shoot. Shi hurriedly ran backward, and his wife, Wan, happened to be in the line of fire. The bullet hit her left breast, and she immediately bled profusely and died in a pool of blood. The bandits then searched and robbed at will, leaving only after an hour. Afterward, Fuji returned home and found his wife dead. Fortunately, his children were unharmed. He checked the stolen items and found that 130 yuan in banknotes and silver dollars, a gold ring, and more than a dozen pieces of clothing had been robbed. In his grief, he went to the city with Tu Zheng Zhou Longhui to report to the county and request an arrest.

Jiangyin Youth Attempts Suicide in Hotel: Fang Yao, from Jiangyin, came to Wuxi from Zhenjiang a few days ago and stayed in Room No. 1 of the Liangxi Hotel on Tongyun Road. In the evening, he ordered the tea room to fetch wine and drank heavily, and also bought five jiao worth of opium. He then wrote two letters, one to Staff Officer Chen of the Hankou Fortress Command and one to Yang Youfu (Fang's maternal uncle) of the Tongyu Caofang outside the North Gate of Jiangyin. After writing the letters, he personally went out to mail them. When he returned to the hotel after 10:00 PM, he closed the door and consumed all the opium and three pre-brought opium pills. He then wrote a letter to his sister-in-law, Fang Huizhen (wife of his fifth elder brother, Fang Juying), and a note to the hotel's accountant, before going to bed to await death. When dawn broke, the neighboring room heard severe moaning and informed the tea room attendant, Chen Gui, who then reported to the accountant. They opened the door and were shocked by what they saw. He was rushed to the hospital for treatment. Fortunately, the poisoning was not deep, and he gradually regained consciousness, so there was no danger to his life. Upon inquiry, it was learned that he took this drastic measure because of his poor circumstances and his previous failed attempts to deal with the anti-smoking investigation.

Chamber of Commerce Resolves on Anti-Japanese Aid to Overseas Chinese Measures: Yesterday, the county chamber of commerce, in response to the anti-Japanese aid to overseas Chinese issue, convened representatives from various industries to discuss the implementation methods. The following resolutions were made: (1) The county party headquarters sent a public letter stating that the Wuxi County People's Anti-Japanese Aid to Overseas Chinese Conference would be held at the Public Sports Ground at 9:00 AM on the 31st of this month. All industries should actively participate and universally fly half-mast flags in mourning. (2) Stopping the import of Japanese goods: The chamber of commerce previously announced to various industries that they should follow Shanghai's procedures. Various industries have also automatically published advertisements to organize inspection teams and handle the registration of Japanese goods. Each trade association should be effectively responsible for starting inspections and immediately conducting investigations and registering Japanese goods. In the future, if any industry is found to be privately importing Japanese goods, the respective trade association should seal the goods and report them to the chamber of commerce for public discussion and strict punishment. (3) Providing relief funds for refugee overseas Chinese: The chamber of commerce will first raise and advance 500 silver dollars and immediately remit them to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce for forwarding, and will also print donation registers and distribute them to various industries for active fundraising.

Business Tax Loan is Extremely Urgent: The county business tax bureau, previously because the provincial government urged the payment of taxes urgently, had no way to raise the funds. The provincial government negotiated with the county chamber of commerce and decided to borrow 30,000 silver dollars as an emergency measure, to be repaid under the county's business tax item. Yang Wufu, the former director of the business tax bureau, received an order from the provincial government to first raise and repay 15,000 silver dollars to the chamber of commerce by the end of this month. After receiving the order, Director Yang immediately sent personnel to various industries to urge the payment of taxes. However, due to the decline in commerce and the occurrence of floods, it was difficult for various industries to raise the funds, so Director Yang was extremely anxious.

Changzhou

New Construction Bureau Chief Arrives in Changzhou: Xu Mojia, the newly appointed construction bureau chief of Wu County, arrived in Changzhou on the evening of the 29th. On the 30th, he met with the former bureau chief, Zhuang Zhongxi, at the Construction Bureau to discuss everything. It is said that he will officially take office on August 1st.

Telegraph Request to Quickly Block Zhenjiang Xiaozhakou: The Wu County Party Headquarters and County Farmers' Association telegraphed the provincial government yesterday, stating that since the beginning of summer, there had been continuous rain, and nearly 80% of the county's fields had been submerged. The autumn harvest was hopeless. Although the rain had subsided slightly, the river water was still rising. The Zhenjiang Xiaozhakou had not yet been blocked, and the river water was pouring in day and night. Farmers in more than a dozen counties below Danyang were bound to be left helpless and awaiting death. They urgently requested the provincial governor to quickly order the Construction Department to send personnel to block the Zhenjiang Xiaozhakou, which would greatly benefit 1.4 million farmers in Jiangnan.

Zhenjiang

Coal Ship Collides and Sinks Wheat Boat: The Tongjin steamship of the Shanghai Haitong Company, towing two iron barges, arrived in Zhenjiang from Shanghai and loaded coal at the Guazhou Zhongxing Company. This afternoon, after it had just finished loading, it first towed one barge out of the inland river. When it reached Chenjiawan, Guazhou, it collided with a barge due to the rapid water flow and unresponsive rudder. The barge, which was loaded with 150 bags of wheat from the Tongyitai firm, sank. Four or five other small boats were swept ashore due to the high water and crashed into the back wall of Xue Xie Mao's kitchen, injuring the owner's wife. Fortunately, her life was not in danger. The incident has been reported to Captain Ding of the Water Police Force, who ordered compensation to be paid.

Gaoyou

Kidnapping Case Occurs in Duxiang Township: The family of Huang Degui, a farmer in Duxiang Township, was suddenly visited by more than a dozen bandits the night before last. After robbing them, they kidnapped his eight-year-old grandson. They then went to the home of Song Guangliang, who lived nearby, and searched it. Because they didn't find much, they also took away his four-year-old son, fired their guns, and fled.

Yuanhe Qianzhuang Closes Down: The financial sector in this county has been severely hit by years of famine. This spring, Jiuda, Fukang, Henghe, Huikangyong, Huikang, and other firms closed down. Unexpectedly, the Yuanhe Qianzhuang outside the North Gate is now also facing financial difficulties and closed down this morning. It is reported that the Huiyuan Qianzhuang outside the North Gate also suspended operations this morning.

Qingjiang

Two Bandit Alarms Recorded Together: Yu Kaifu, who has lived behind the Gongmao Supervision Station in Xiba Town, District 3 of Huaiyin, for many years, is not well-off. At 10:00 PM on the 23rd, six bandits suddenly carrying sharp weapons went to Yu's house to search and rob. Finally, they also abducted Yu Kaifu's wife. The town's Public Security First Branch and the Salt Affairs Escort Team heard the alarm and tried to rescue her, but the bandits had already fled southwest. Also, on the morning of the 25th, Deng Jiandi, the captain of the Second Squadron of the Huaiyin Police, reported to the brigade headquarters that Sun Huazeng, the town head of Lao Zhangji, and patrolman Wang Sichun had reported that the people in Lao Zhangji, Daxing'an, Zhangzhuang, Shazhuang, and other areas were fleeing to the county seat due to a large group of bandits from Shu. They requested that troops be sent to defend and suppress them. Commander Fu immediately sent personnel to Yugou Town, ordering Li Xiumin, the captain of the Third Squadron, to lead his team to assist.

Yellow Water Floods Sicheng Gate: The silted Yellow River in the old Tong Siyang county town usually has no water, and all the river beaches and riverbeds are used by local people to grow agricultural products. This year, the water volume has increased sharply, and the continuous rain has caused the silted Yellow River to be more than ten feet deep, flooding in all directions, gradually flowing inward from Simen. The people of Sicheng used cattail bags to hold soil and separately stacked the four city gates into small embankments. Therefore, the current situation in Siyang County can be described as being in the water.

Shaoxing

Provincial Loan Signing Scheduled: The 200,000 yuan provincial loan for the Shaoxing silver and money industry has been agreed upon by the county bureau director and representatives of the industry. The treaty will be signed on the 31st. The banking industry will borrow 60,000 yuan, and the money industry will borrow 140,000 yuan.

Mingguang

Major Flooding on the Southern Section of the Jinpu Railway Destroys Roads: The southern section of the Jinpu Railway is relatively low-lying, and traffic is often affected when the river floods. Earlier this month, the Huai and Chi Rivers rose, flooding the tracks near Linhuai and south of Mingguang. At that time, vehicles could still pass by probing the water. Unexpectedly, the accumulated water had not yet receded when there was heavy rain again, and mountain floods rushed down, causing the river to rise again. In addition to Mingguang and Linhuai, which were still in their previous state, the road between Dongge and Huaqiying was washed away. Since the 26th, trains have been unable to pass. The railway bureau ordered workers to rush to repair it, but it was difficult to achieve results due to the deep water and rapid flow. Today, the southbound fifth-class ticket train was blocked in Chuzhou, and was subsequently changed to the sixth-class train to open north. After the first express train arrived in Bengbu, it was also changed to the second-class train and returned to Tianjin. According to railway news, if the road workers cannot repair it in time, the trains will be divided into two sections: Pukou to Huaqiying and Tianjin to Chuzhou, with ferries temporarily maintaining traffic in the middle. As for the flooded sections of the road around Mingguang and Linhuai, stones are currently being transported to build embankments to prevent any unexpected events.

Fengtai

Banditry Rampant Amidst Flooding: Fengtai in northern Anhui is located near the Huai River and has always been prone to flooding. Since the beginning of spring and summer, there has been continuous rain everywhere, and the rivers in Feng County have risen sharply. Low-lying areas have become wetlands, and embankments along the river have been broken in many places. The water in the plains is more than ten feet deep. Reed huts have collapsed, and stored grain and firewood have floated away with the water. Many people and animals have drowned, and the autumn harvest has been completely destroyed. The disaster victims are wailing and have no homes to return to. They sleep in the open air, exposed to the wind and eat meagerly, and their cries echo across the fields. It is truly tragic. Before the flood disaster has been relieved, banditry has risen again. The northeast townships of the county have always been areas where bandits are produced. Recently, several hundred bandits have gathered in the Tianjiaji area, occupying the place and being extremely rampant. Nearby villages have been looted, burned, and people have been kidnapped. They have done everything. A few days ago, many bandit ships suddenly arrived in Sujiagang and looted extensively, kidnapping several hostages, cutting off both ears of village head Su Qizhi, and shooting him in the water. It is terrible to hear. The bandits are now numerous and have threatened to attack Feng County. Upon receiving the report, the county authorities urgently convened a local emergency meeting to prepare for self-defense.

Education News

Important News

Higher Academies of Various Provinces Established by the Former Qing Ministry of Education

Since the Ministry of Education strictly reviewed the qualifications of school graduates, graduates of unregistered private schools are not qualified to enroll in higher education or serve in various institutions. Their qualifications are also affected when the Ministry of Personnel reviews them. However, schools that have been registered by the current Ministry of Education and the former Beijing Ministry of Education have verifiable records. For schools run in the former Qing Dynasty, it is quite difficult to verify them. The Ministry of Education has repeatedly approved inquiries from the Ministry of Personnel and the Examination Yuan regarding the qualifications and level of graduates from higher academies in various provinces. The Ministry of Education has verified the higher academies of various provinces registered by the Ministry of Education in the former Qing Dynasty based on the files of the Beiping Archives Preservation Office. They are listed below: Zhili Higher Academy (ceased operation in 1913), Shuntian Higher Academy (ceased operation in 1912), Fengtian Higher Academy (merged into the Politics and Law School in 1912, no graduates in regular courses), Imperial Clan Eight Banners Higher Academy (ceased operation in 1912), Jiangshi Higher Academy (ceased operation in 1911), Jiangsu Higher Academy (ceased operation in 1912), Anhui Higher Academy (ceased operation in 1914),

Jiangxi Higher Academy (ceased operation in 1912), Zhejiang Higher Academy (ceased operation in 1914), Fujian Higher Academy (ceased operation in 1914), Hunan Higher Academy (ceased operation in 1912), Sichuan Higher Academy (ceased operation in 1916), Henan Higher School (ceased operation in 1914), Henan Keji Higher Academy (no records in the Republic of China), Shandong Higher Academy (ceased operation in 1914), Shandong Keji Higher Academy (no records in the Republic of China), Gansu Higher Academy (ceased operation in 1912), Xinjiang Higher Academy (changed to a middle school in 1908 and did not offer higher regular courses), Guangdong Higher Academy (ceased operation in 1913), Shaanxi Higher Academy (ceased operation in 1912, no graduates in regular courses), Guangxi Higher Academy (ceased operation in 1914, no graduates in regular courses), Shaanxi Hongdao Higher Academy (only offered middle school classes and did not offer higher regular courses, changed to a middle industrial school in 1909), Yunnan Higher Academy (only offered middle school classes and did not offer higher regular courses), Manchu and Mongolian Higher Academy (established by the Ministry of Education in 1907), Zhibian Academy (graduates in 1911 were verified by the Ministry of Education and given awards according to the Legal and Political Special Department), Jing Shi Higher Industrial Academy established by the Ministry of Agriculture, Industry and Commerce (renamed National Industrial Vocational School after the founding of the Republic of China), Shanghai Higher Industrial Academy established by the Ministry of Posts and Communications (renamed Shanghai Industrial Vocational School of the Ministry of Communications after 1919), Jiangnan Higher Industrial Academy (ceased operation in 1913), Hunan Higher Industrial Academy (renamed Hunan Public Industrial Vocational School after the founding of the Republic of China), Fengtian Higher Industrial Academy (preparatory courses were offered first at the time of establishment, and in 1909 the Ministry of Education ordered the preparatory courses to be changed to a middle industrial school), Zhili Higher Industrial Academy (renamed Zhili Public Industrial Vocational School after the founding of the Republic of China), Liangguang Higher Industrial Academy (ceased operation in 1911, no higher graduates), Zhili Higher Agricultural Academy (renamed Zhili Public Agricultural Vocational School after the founding of the Republic of China), Hubei Higher Agricultural Academy (renamed Hubei Higher Agriculture and Forestry School after the founding of the Republic of China, ceased operation three years later), Shandong Higher Agricultural Academy (renamed Shandong Public Agricultural Vocational School after the founding of the Republic of China), Shanxi Higher Agriculture and Forestry Academy (Republic of China)

Renamed Shanxi Public Agricultural Vocational School), Jiangxi Higher Agricultural Academy (renamed Jiangxi Public Agricultural Vocational School after the founding of the Republic of China), Zhejiang Higher Agricultural Academy (no records in the Republic of China), Zhili Higher Commercial Academy (middle school classes were offered first at the time of establishment, renamed Zhili Public Commercial Vocational School after the founding of the Republic of China), Jiangnan Higher and Secondary Commercial Academy (attached special courses in banking and customs, graduates who completed three years of study were approved by the Ministry as equivalent to the Legal and Political Special Department, no records after 1913), Hunan Private Mingde Academy added a higher commercial specialized course (renamed Mingde University in the Republic of China and moved to Beijing). Explanation: (1) Except for Mingde Academy, which was private, the rest were all government-run. However, most of the seals used did not have the words "government-run." (2) Except for the Shuntian and Eight Banners Academies, which were established with the approval of the Ministry of Education, the rest were directly established with the approval of the various ministries or governors of the provinces. The existing old records of the academies have undergone reforms and relocations, and are no longer complete. Moreover, the period when the academies were established was mostly before the establishment of the Ministry of Education (the edict to establish the Ministry of Education was issued in the winter of 1905, and it was roughly established in 1906. Therefore, the Ministry of Education's files mostly date back to 1906 and cannot accurately determine the year in which each academy was registered. However, the establishment of regular courses in each academy was approved by the Ministry of Education. (3) All those called "Higher Academy of a certain province" (from Zhili to Yunnan), without the words "industrial," "agricultural," or "commercial," had a curriculum equivalent to a three-year university preparatory course. The admission qualifications were limited to middle school graduates, the length of study was three years, and the graduation awards were given the status of juren and a real official position (those ranked highest were given the position of secretary of the Grand Secretariat for domestic use, or prefect for external use; those ranked excellent were given the position of secretary of the Secretariat Department for domestic use, or county magistrate for external use; those ranked average were given the position of department director of the ministry or temple for domestic use, or sub-prefect for external use). Also, in the former Qing Dynasty, this type of higher academy was also an independent academy. Its admission qualifications, length of study, and graduate treatment were the same as those of higher industrial academies or higher industrial and commercial academies. After the establishment of the Republic of China, the education system was revised, and the Ministry of Education instructed all provinces to send students of this type of higher academy to the national university preparatory course or to continue until graduation. Therefore, this type of higher academy mostly ceased operation in the early years of the Republic of China. However, in the early years of the Republic of China, the university preparatory course still used a three-year system. In 1917, the length of the university undergraduate course was extended and the length of the university preparatory course was shortened to two years, and this type of school disappeared. In short, this type of higher academy and the three-year university preparatory course, in terms of qualifications and length of study, were equivalent to vocational schools, but in terms of curriculum, they were not vocational in nature. Compared to the current high school system, they were superior (the former Qing Dynasty middle school was five years, plus three years of higher academy, for a total of eight years, so it was superior to the current high school system). (4) All higher industrial academies and higher agricultural, industrial, and commercial academies had specialized curricula. The admission qualifications were limited to middle school graduates, and the length of study was three years, except for the agricultural department of the Higher Agricultural Academy, which was four years, while the forestry department was still three years. The graduation awards were given the status of juren and a real official position. After the founding of the Republic of China, in addition to being renamed various vocational schools in accordance with regulations, most of the others for which there were no records in the Republic of China had ceased operation.

This order."

Jiangsu Education Department Rewards Academic Works of Education Institution Personnel

In order to promote academic research, the Jiangsu Education Department has specially formulated interim measures to reward academic works of incumbent teachers and staff members of educational institutions in the province. It was submitted to the 364th meeting of the Provincial Government Committee and approved for implementation. All academic works and teaching lectures of current education service personnel in the province that can be published as separate volumes may be sent to the department for review. The reward methods are divided into the following three categories: (1) Introduce them in the Provincial Government Gazette and various publications of the Department of Education to promote them, or issue a circular to all educational institutions in the province to adopt them. (2) The Department of Education issues a certificate of award to encourage them. (3) For particularly outstanding works or lectures, after review by experts, they are awarded bonuses in three grades: A (300 yuan), B (200 yuan), and C (100 yuan). It is reported that the applicants are very enthusiastic, and no less than 100 kinds of works have been submitted to the department for review. The department originally set the deadline for collection at the end of July, and experts will be hired for review as soon as the deadline is reached.

The deadline for the department's reward for academic works by students studying abroad is set for the end of October of this year.

Two Newly Published Sports Books

(1) Sports Field Guide

(2) A Brief History of World Sports

—Published by Qin Fen Book Company—

—Creations from the Sports World—

The Qin Fen Book Company at No. 39 Xinmin Village, Ma Lang Road, French Concession, Shanghai, has recently compiled and published various sports books to promote domestic sports. Previous publications such as "Football and Basketball Training Methods" and "Football Rules and Questions and Answers" have been excellent, popular throughout the country, and praised by the times. It is now learned that two new books, "Sports Field Guide" and "A Brief History of World Sports," have been published. The content is excellent, rich, and complete. "Sports Field Guide" is written by Wang Zhuangfei, director of the Shanghai No. 1 Public Sports Field, who has been involved in sports field management for more than ten years. It emphasizes both theory and practice, and provides detailed descriptions of the strategies, equipment, construction, organization, management, and work progress of sports field management. It also includes dozens of various charts and diagrams on organization and construction for further explanation. Furthermore, the entire book is based on China's current situation, incorporating Western strengths and developing solutions suitable for China's actual environment, making it most suitable for modern China's needs and applications. It is not only a guide for sports field managers across the country, but also a must-have book for sports school students and sports researchers. The price is 70 cents per copy, now a special price of 10% off, 63 cents (2 cents postage per copy, 6 cents for registration). The other book, "A Brief History of World Sports," is written by Zhang Jiwu, director of physical education at Nankai University, who has been working in the sports world for more than ten years. This book provides a well-founded and systematic account of the state of sports in China and the West since history. It covers the origins of sports, the dark ages, and the development process, and provides separate explanations for sports in various countries, with particular detail on China. Therefore, this book is the most detailed record of Chinese and Western sports history and also marks its beginning. All sports professionals and students across the country should have this compilation to thoroughly understand the process of world sports and serve as a basis for improving Chinese sports and promoting sports models. The entire book is well-printed, the price is 60 cents per copy, a special price of 10% off, 54 cents (1 cent postage per copy, 6 cents for registration). The general distributor is Qin Fen Book Company, with a retail department at Xie Wenyi, Wangping Street, Sanma Road. Shanghai retail locations include the Civilization Book Company on Nanjing Road, the World Book Company and Datong Book Company on Sima Road, the Qixin Book Company on Qipan Street, and the Chinese National Sports Association on LaoShenfu Road, the No. 1 Public Sports Field in West City, Standard Sports Company, Huadong Sichuan Road Mihualian Store, and other sports companies on Central Road.

Free Talk

A Word of Wisdom

— Yi Mei

▲The ability of art to move people lies in craftsmanship and natural interest. Intricate changes reach the realm of divine subtlety.

▲Reading books requires understanding them thoroughly. Doing things requires being practical.

▲Yang Shuzi wore light fur and a loose belt, and Zhuge Liang held a feather fan and a silk scarf. What a detached attitude, yet how passionate their careers were.

The heroes of the world should take them as their model.

▲Thrifty writers waste paper and ink. Incompetent people waste effort and money.

▲Rather than uttering platitudes, it is better to be silent like a golden man.

▲Being indifferent to fame and wealth naturally leads to leisure and comfort.

▲Building a small house provides a place to sit and lie down. Storing a few books allows one to recite and read. What more could one ask for in this floating life?

▲Tired of the noise of the city, yet unable to escape it. Envying the joy of the mountains and forests, yet unable to settle there.

▲It is okay to mention worries and sorrows in poetry and prose, but it should be felt and expressed, not moaning without illness.

▲The cost of living increases year by year. However, today's prices will surely be considered cheap and delightful ten years from now.

▲The higher the breasts of modern women, the greater their power to attract the opposite sex.

▲The joy of losing something beloved and then finding it again is indescribable.

▲Passing summer, one says winter is good. Passing winter, one says summer is good. Those who are not in the situation admire it. Those who are in the situation despise it. This is the psychology of ordinary people.

▲Wearing rubber overshoes is stuffy and does not allow sweat to evaporate. After finishing work and returning home, one should quickly remove shoes and socks and sit barefoot in the wind. Is this not delightful?

Strange Stone Artifacts of Chengdu

— Zhang Yan

▲Stone abacus can be used for calculation ▲Stone instruments can be played

About twenty miles outside the West Gate of Chengdu, there is a place called Wujia Linzi in Xipu Field. The area is lush with trees and the scenery is beautiful and secluded. Amidst the green trees, there is a stone dwelling built by a certain person's individual effort. The beams, rafters, walls, window lattices, and lintels are all made of stone, with exquisite carvings and unique ingenuity. The fish, insects, flowers, birds, beasts, and flying fowl carved on the walls are all lifelike and seem to leap and live. The most peculiar thing is that the stone abacus carved on the wall has beads that can all move, and a dry tobacco pipe can be filled with tobacco and smoked. There is also a birdcage carved, protruding from the stone surface, with a stone trough and a stone platform inside. A bird stands on the platform, opening its mouth and flapping its wings as if to sing. There is also a stone lion, with hair patterns all over its body like silk, thin and delicate. The eyes are bright and full of spirit. The lion's mouth holds a ball. When you probe it with your hand, although it can rotate freely, you can never take it out. What is even more peculiar is that on the stone railing pillars of the garden fishpond, each top is carved with a fat baby, some holding sheng, some holding conch shells, some holding flutes, and some holding whistles. When tourists blow them, they can all make sounds one by one. Musicians can even play them with ups and downs, it is said.

New Method of Nourishing Qi and Killing Mosquitoes

— Huang Yingdai

▲A Major Invention by American Scientists

The season of lotus and summer has arrived. Mosquitoes and insects are most easily bred, disturbing people's work and invading people's sweet dreams. They are annoying. We have no way to eliminate them. Now, Cornell University in the United States has contributed a new method of catching mosquitoes for us. If we adopt this method, all mosquitoes and insects will not be difficult to eliminate completely. We can work safely and sleep soundly. Isn't that pleasant? Where there are larvae in lakes and swamps, it is where mosquitoes breed. However, these larvae can be captured and destroyed by using oxygen (oxygen). Oxygen is indispensable for the lives of various animals, but now it can kill mosquitoes. Isn't that strange? The experimental site is in the forest within Cornell's borders. There is a pond. Since using oxygen to kill mosquitoes, mosquitoes have disappeared. It has been several years. It is said that in ponds where mosquitoes breed, there must be a kind of aquatic plant called Chara. It grows on the bottom of the water, and mosquito eggs parasitize on it. Later, Dr. Mason and Professor Hugh Mun of Cornell University discovered that once mosquito eggs parasitize on this plant, all oxygen bubbles gradually disappear. Therefore, after the female mosquito lays eggs, this plant still grows, and larvae are not produced. However, after withering, mosquito colonies can breed. From this alone, it can be seen that the presence or absence of oxygen has a considerable relationship with the reproduction of mosquito eggs. Therefore, several glass jars were used, filled with water, half containing oxygen bubbles and half without. Mosquito food was also placed in the jars, and 50 larvae were placed in the jars. After a few days, mosquitoes were formed in the jars without oxygen bubbles in turn, while those with oxygen bubbles died completely. Over time, the mosquito killing rate of oxygen reached 100%. It can be seen that oxygen is sufficient to kill mosquitoes. Now the doctors are doing further research to use oxygen bubbles to completely kill the larvae in the pond, so that mosquitoes cannot grow. However, the principle of oxygen killing mosquitoes has not yet been reported in detail by them.

A Cooling Off Record at Wuyou Park

— Zhe Cun

The location for cooling off in the hot summer does not necessarily have to be a tall building, a waterside pavilion, or a windy pavilion. It only needs to be a place between the village and the suburbs, where land is developed and houses are built, with three parts water and two parts bamboo. However, the more trees there are, the better. Sitting and whistling in it, one feels quiet, clean, and free from worldly dust, making it the best place to escape the summer heat. Wuyou Park is located in the northwest corner of the town, close to the west bank of the Chuanchang River, covering an area of about sixty or seventy acres. It is surrounded by lively clear water, and a bow-shaped plank bridge leads to it. There is a bridge pavilion on it, with railings decorated in blue and white. The tree shade on the left and right of the park gate sometimes brushes the bridge body. From a distance, it is picturesque. There are thousands of trees, mostly elm, willow, pine, and locust trees. They are all more than several feet high, circling the park in an unbroken intertwining manner. A three-bay Matsutake Pavilion is built in the north to receive the southern breeze. A pond is located dozens of steps in front of the Matsutake Pavilion, with various aquatic plants planted in it. To the west is the Mo'an Villa, surrounded by short trees, as if it were a separate path, with silk and bamboo instruments and chess boards for recreation. To the south, there is a high mound with a pavilion built on it, formerly called the Zuiweng Pavilion, but now renamed the Zhongshan Pavilion. Climbing up and viewing the scenery, both near and far, can be counted. The roads in the park are winding and circular, with tall trees on both sides of the road. Tourists walking in it are like opening an umbrella, almost forgetting the suffering of the scorching heat on the dusty road. A few plots of land are also divided for gardeners to cultivate, making one feel a sense of farming in the flowers and trees, and a sense of mountains and forests in the mortal world. This is what Liu Zihou meant by "looking at its planting, it is clear, beautiful, spreading, and comfortable; looking at its storage, it is melting, rippling, and winding." The villagers have recently proposed to expand the construction. In the future, it can be more perfect. Although I have been a native of this town for generations, I am lazy to travel. The other day, I went for a walk alone and stayed for a short time. There are also people selling tea and snacks inside, which is very convenient for tourists. I sat silently for a while, and a long wind suddenly came, and the surroundings sounded like waves, or like a waterfall, or like a stream. It was sometimes mixed with the sound of tea being brewed. At this moment, all worldly worries disappeared, and I seemed to have entered a cool country. I got a sentence: "Walking along the dike, tired of traveling, I took a short stay in the shade of green trees. Fish and birds are close to people and all feel comfortable. From time to time, I hear the sound of splashing and hooks." Near the end of June, Xinwei, I returned and wrote it down, hoping not to forget the traces of my footsteps at that time.

A Few Questions

— Mei Er

A ethicist came up with a few questions as follows. "A hard-working parents gave birth to a romantic son, who married a virtuous daughter-in-law. What is this family like?"

"A singer admired by thousands of people. A is willing to marry her. B is willing to marry her. C and D are also willing to marry her. In the end, which kind of person should she choose as her life partner?"

"The singer chose a romantic teenager after thousands of selections. Later, the teenager's original wife suddenly ran to the door. Please teach me how to deal with it."

"On the one hand, he bragged to his lover about how rich he was, but he happened to run into his original wife and his father. In an helpless situation, how should he deal with it?"

"The facts were exposed. The wife knew that her husband was having an affair. What else would she do?"

"The facts were exposed. Qingren knew that the person she chose was a big bastard. What else would she do?"

"When people die, will things be over?"

The above many questions are not imagined out of thin air, but are produced on a fact. However, its answer is by no means imaginable by smart readers. Now, Tianyi Film Company has decided to solve these many problems in order to make the first domestic film movie. On the surface, the urban life is written vividly, making people feel novel and lively when they see it. But in essence, its lesson is worthy of being seen by the entire Chinese people. What exactly does a story inside satirize? There are enthusiastic and sad songs in the film, romantic and intense dances, and moving and funny twists and turns of the bizarre layout. Although its premiere is still pending, its name is "Song Market Spring Colors." It is worth remembering. Wait and see how it solves the above problems in the future.

Travel Notes from India (70)

— Linghua

In India, all Hindus will celebrate a two-day festival starting tomorrow, and a meeting is held tonight. Men and women gather together. Carpets are laid on the ground. The ceremony of scattering flower garlands is performed first. I also participate. A class leader leads the recitation of ancient Sanskrit poems. Wood is burned in a basin, and oil is poured onto it while reciting. It seems to be a custom of worshipping fire. Then, a large group of students sing, led by one student. He sings a phrase first, then everyone sings together. The sound is clear, melodious, and transcendent. I don’t know what song it is. It is accompanied by drums. Then, music is played. Each person sings folk songs in various languages at will. They also invite me to recite Chinese poems, which they greatly appreciate. When I listen to Indian music, songs, and poems, I don’t understand the words, but I appreciate the sounds. In general, they are beyond what China can achieve. The beauty stems from diligent learning. Their Buddhist and Brahman philosophy is already higher than human understanding. When this is expressed in music and songs, the tones are lofty and transcendent, incomparable to the mundane world. In China, the highest form of song is the Ya and Song sections of the Three Hundred Songs, which are about the way of kings. Going further back to the times of Tang and Yu, it reaches the way of emperors. Only immortals can play music that transcends the ordinary, comparable to a part of Indian music. But its vastness and profundity are beyond China's realm. Try listening to the chants of monks; they can transport people to other realms. If the songs of Chu in China could be set to music, their realm would also be very high. After the students sing, they distribute sugar and perform the red dot on the forehead ceremony. They also put a dot on my forehead. Finally, they sing a patriotic song and disperse. The moonlit night is exceptionally beautiful. The educator, Narun Yesha, wishes success to the Asian Cultural Union.

After the meeting ends, the students gather to discuss the future of Asia and the Gandhian movement. Gandhi's title is "Mahatma," the same word used to refer to the Buddha in the past. The Buddha was also called "Mahatma." The students say that according to Hindus, the Buddha was the ninth Buddha, and Gandhi is the tenth Buddha. I ask about Gandhi's policies and the effectiveness they have achieved among the people. The students say that Indians have no weapons, so they focus on economic efforts. There are three strategies: First, not using foreign goods. The annual savings are already in the hundreds of millions. British merchants are in great difficulty, and some are demanding that the British government grant Indians freedom to restore trade. This shows their predicament. Second, strikes. Not providing services to foreigners for any projects. The British must have Indians do everything. This is not easy to achieve, only a part can be done. Third, tax resistance. This is very difficult. In Gugrat, a city near Mumbai, Gandhi's hometown, they are working hard on tax resistance. The police burned their houses and killed their people, so people abandoned their fields and fled. This movement is happening everywhere, but it has not yet been very successful. However, the police are all Indians and are gradually showing signs of going slow. Even the soldiers are gradually showing signs of being slow. Over time, they will gain the sympathy of everyone, and changes will naturally occur. Many women and children are joining the movement. In short, tax resistance is happening everywhere. The British cannot arrest so many people. This strategy is very important. If they can cut off the British economic source, the troops cannot be supported, and the power of the government will gradually weaken. This is Gandhi's movement strategy. In any case, Indians will fight for freedom until death, and will not stop until they get freedom.

Rotary Club Lecture

Women, Women (5)

— Yao Suifeng

The young shop assistant spoke as he walked. Mr. Lu did not say a word, silently following behind him as he entered. The people inside heard the sounds from outside and hurried out. With the same surprise, they said, "Xiao Rong! Is that you back?"

Mr. Lu awkwardly uttered the proper form of address: "Dad! Mom!" He handed the bunch of bananas he was carrying to his mother. His mother was extremely happy. She saw that her son had grown up so much, even though he had only been gone for less than half a year. But it seemed as if he had brought back boundless happiness. His father was naturally very happy as well because he had worked hard for most of his life, placing all his hopes on his son. He usually silently prayed that his son would study hard so that he could honor his ancestors and bring glory to the family. Now that his son had returned from school, although he had not yet graduated, his hopes seemed to have taken a further step, a deeper level.

Once inside the house, his mother busily wiped a chair with her sleeve, telling him to sit down. She also hurriedly called for tea to be poured, water to be boiled, and snacks to be bought. She treated him earnestly, as if he were a distinguished guest. Meanwhile, his father also felt at a loss for words, haphazardly asking about the situation at school: "Is the schoolwork busy? Are there many classmates?..."

Mr. Lu not only forgot to ask his parents, "Are you well?" and "Is business good?" but he also forgot someone else until he saw someone carrying a bowl of noodles out of the kitchen. He seemed stunned.

With the same surprise, she said, "Xiao Rong! Is that you back?"

He really did not want to see this last person who came out, his wife of three years. But he managed to change his contemptuous expression into one that seemed very gentle, and he said, "How are you? Are you at home?"

"It's been raining for several days, business is very slow, I haven't gone out for two days, I didn't expect you to be back!" She revealed the most joyful expression, as if she had received infinite comfort from her husband.

So she sat down, and the bowl of noodles was delivered from her hands to her husband's face. "You must be hungry! If it's not enough, there's more!" she said with a smile.

"Is it too bland? Do you want some soy sauce?" She was still speaking attentively. She stood up and took a basin and brought out some water.

Mr. Lu took one bite and stopped eating. He said, "I'm very full, I can't eat any more!"

▲ Sentiment Turns Bearish, Breaking the Forty Tael Barrier

Yesterday, the 30th, the gold price continued its sharp decline. The morning saw a rise, but it weakened in the afternoon, with some ups and downs in between. July Marked Yarn Settlement Process

▲ Settlement Price 164 Taels... Volume 9,100 Bales

July marked yarn originally had the power to rise because the northern route genuinely needed large-scale development, morale was good, and the situation was gradually improving. Unexpectedly, a certain merchant took advantage of the rising price to sell off a large quantity, reversing the market, and creating a rather unstable situation. The price fell from 162-3 taels to below 57 taels, which shows the heavy pressure from large households. Before long, the Wanbaoshan Incident was discovered, causing considerable damage to Korean residents. Economic severance with Japan and patriotic movements became increasingly heated. Refusal of goods began as a result. The spot yarn market became very tight, and prices rose slightly. 42-count fine yarn surged by dozens of taels, and people were shocked. Speculators flocked in, and buying sentiment pervaded the market. The rising trend intensified, and the price even broke through 60 taels outside the customs, reaching a maximum of 164 taels and 6 mace. However, certain manufacturers continued to sell, while another manufacturer bought low and went long. The two sides were evenly matched. In the final round, the bid was raised to 5 taels, but because large households sold again, it went lower, resulting in 4 taels. The settlement price was 164 taels, with a remainder of 9,100 bales, of which 4,500 bales were actually settled, and the rest were settled independently. This included 100 bales of 10-count Red Kuixing, 1,500 bales of Cai Kuixing, 50 bales of Golden Rooster, 900 bales of Hongfu, 1,350 bales of Three Sheep, 700 bales of Shi Yi, 100 bales of Earth, 50 bales of Fugui, and 200 bales of Red Lotus Bee. Both parties in the settlement were manufacturers. The numbers and bale amounts of each firm are recorded below:

Overview of July Chinese Marked Yarn Settlement

▲ Settlement Price 38 Taels... Volume 30,100 Piculs

At the beginning of the month, the market sentiment for July Chinese marked yarn was unusually soft, mainly because the overseas cotton market was weak and sluggish, and the price of gold was also fluctuating, which made people more apprehensive. The actual needs of various factories were sluggish and there was no digestion at all. Moreover, the yarn market was trending downward, so the market presented a situation of hesitation, between 38 and 39 taels. However, Japanese merchants continued to drag in a long position and did not relax. Later, due to poor yarn prices and unstable American cotton, the market broke through the 9-fen mark, and morale once became weak, reaching a low of 37 taels and 2 mace. Subsequently, as Japanese merchants took delivery, the market rebounded slightly. In the end, the price of the last round was 38 taels, the settlement price was 38 taels, and the remainder was 30,100 piculs. The goods were of two types: Shaanxi and Huoji flower. Shenchang delivered 6,600 piculs, Hengyi 4,100 piculs, and Xinxing 2,500 piculs, which was the most. Grains: Changshu & Wuxi Early Season Japonica Rice Bids Up by Half a Yuan

▲ Due to hoarding in warehouses

▲ Xin Zha: Yesterday, boats from inland areas, including Wuxi, Jiangyin, Changzhou, Yixing, Tongli, Shipu, Xitang, etc., numbered seventeen or eighteen. Trading in the market was initially sluggish but then became active. Changshu and Wuxi early season Japonica rice slightly increased in warehouses, estimated at two to three thousand piculs. Prices bid up by 5 jiao. Early and late rice were sold as soon as they arrived, so the trend tightened by 3 jiao. Tongbian and Yinhua types opened steadily. Luyang Jian and Bu Jian rice were slow to move. The market trend was high because foreign rice was still weak, following lower by a few jiao.

▲ South Market: Yesterday, sources from various gangs arrived infrequently, mainly from Pinghu and Nangang gangs. Retail sales in urban and rural stores were not active. Thick Japonica rice arrived and sales were slow, and the price remained the same. Only five or six boats of thin rice arrived, and sales were not active. There was a slight outlet in this street, and the price did not rise or fall. Luyang Jian rice was not popular, and the price was lower by one or two jiao. It is said that foreign rice is being used to supply military rations, so there is some movement, and the price has hardened by half a yuan.

The Flour Market Situation is Severe Before Settlement

Yesterday, the flour market situation was still very severe. Because there was only one trading day this month, short sellers outside the industry had to cover their positions according to the trend. Because spot goods could be bid up, manufacturers were unwilling to deliver more. Buyers were very firm, and there was no short squeeze on the 29th. Forward months were still being bought up by inland gangs, and the highest price rose by more than 2 fen compared to the previous day. However, because Fuxin, Fufeng, Xinda, and other factories were selling off, it fell by 1 fen, but it was still better than the closing price of the previous day. As a result, this month rose by 2.5 fen compared to the previous day, August by 1.75 fen, September by 1 fen, October by 1.5 fen, November by 1.25 fen, and December by 0.5 fen.

Wheat Futures Rose in the Morning and Fell in the Afternoon

Due to rumors of more foreign wheat being contracted, with three or four ships.

Spot wheat arrivals are not numerous, bidding up by three or four fen.

Yesterday, after the opening of wheat futures, the market for each month, although the weather caused absorption, the near and far months were better by three or four fen than the previous day. By the time the market opened in the afternoon, the opening prices for each month fell sharply again. It was rumored that two major factories, so and so, had successively contracted three or four ships of Australian No. 3 wheat at a combined price of 4 taels, 2 mace, and 6 fen, causing people to panic and fall back down. September fell by as much as 9 fen compared to the highest price in the morning. Given this situation, if the standard price is excessively raised, it will give foreign wheat more opportunities to increase its imports to China. As a result, August fell by 2 fen compared to the previous day, September fell by 6 fen, October fell by 3 fen, November fell by 1 fen, and December did not move. Because spot wheat arrivals are not numerous and the producing areas are also rising step by step, each grade has also been bid up by three or four fen. As a result, Shuangfeng wheat was 3 taels, 6 mace, and 8 fen, followed by 3 taels, 5 mace, and 5 fen, 3 taels, 5 mace, and 9 fen, and Danyang wheat was 3 taels and 7 mace, totaling 2,500 bags, which were reportedly purchased by Fuxin, Huafeng, and Xinda.

July Soybean Futures Short Squeeze Temporarily Ceased

▲ Settled at a price of 5 taels, 4 mace, and 5 fen.

Dalian soybeans were supposed to be auctioned until yesterday, but because of the short squeeze in this month, the auction was stopped the day before yesterday. The long side, after discussing with the directors and relevant brokers, settled all short accounts at a price of 5 taels, 4 mace, and 5 fen. It is said that this short squeeze was not intentional, but because the receiver was reportedly a manufacturer, and the short accounts were all outsiders, with no goods to deliver, they had to suffer an invisible loss.

Silk and Tea: Zhenmei Green Tea Trading is Brisk

Yesterday, English and French firms were actively searching for Zhenmei green tea from Wuyuan, Tunxi, and other areas. Trading was unusually brisk, and the market was slightly firmer than before. Currently, there are few low-grade Zhenmei teas left on the market, and there are only a little over ten thousand boxes of medium and high-grade goods. Chinese tea merchants are taking a firm stance, and the market price is expected to rise. The stock of Zhenmei and Xiumei teas is thin, and the selling price has continued to rise by three or four taels. However, Russian firms have not yet started to purchase Gongxi tea, and Baitu Zhuang tea is not very popular, which has affected green tea somewhat.

Chinese Silk Merchants Unanimously Refuse to Use Japanese Cocoons

This year, both spring and summer silkworm crops in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have had surprisingly good harvests. The raw materials of silk factories in various ports have long been insufficient for reeling, so they are all promoting farmers to raise autumn silkworms to make up for the shortage. However, because Japanese merchants believe that this year's cocoon production in their country is still abundant and the cocoon price is not cheap, they are all transporting large quantities of Japanese cocoons to China for sale. Since the start of economic severance with Japan, Japanese merchants have been trying to sell large quantities of Japanese cocoons stored in Yokohama and other ports. Because Chinese silk merchants are eager to be patriotic, they have already decided to unanimously refuse to use Japanese cocoons. Therefore, recently, no one has inquired about Japanese cocoons. As a result, they will still be transported back to Japan or transferred to other countries for sale.

Foreign Firms' Silk Sales are Lifeless

Yesterday, the overseas market for Chinese silk was all quotations and no sales. Telegrams were not forwarded, and the market was sluggish. Yesterday, only Xinfu and others imported 15 bales of Baiqian silk, and Meida and others imported 8 bales of Huangcu silk. The prices were all firm.

Piece Goods: Coarse Cloth Gradually Rises

▲ East goods are still being shipped out every day... the selling price has risen instead.

▲ Local Cloth: The price has risen very quickly in recent days, mainly because the boycott of Japanese goods is becoming increasingly tense, and the sales of Chinese goods have suddenly become smooth. Coarse cloth is particularly firm and expensive. Yesterday, 9-pound cloth was 5 taels and 2 mace leaving the customs, and 10-pound Blue Chicken had reached 5 taels and 5 mace. 11-pound goods, Jardine Matheson's Three Deer, Three Rabbit, and Three Cat were all 5 taels, 7 mace, and 5 fen. 16-pound Five Crane and Peony were all over 8 taels and 1 mace. Fine cloth Chinese goods are very scarce. Fine twill Jincheng has sold for 8 taels, 2 mace, and 5 fen, and Butterfly Ball for 7 taels, 7 mace, and 5 fen. However, fine cloth and fine twill from Japanese factories have not fallen at all, because although inspections have been implemented in Shanghai, foreign ports have not yet boycotted them, and there are still many transactions.

▲ East and West Piece Goods: Yesterday, both the quoted and Zhuang goods of Western goods rose by three or four qian. However, there is an abnormal shortage of ordinary colors in the market, so East goods are still secretly active. Many are being shipped out for export every day. Not only has the price not fallen, but it has risen instead. Yesterday, Yuehua velvet was shipped away by the Changjiang Gang in large quantities. Large pattern velvet was 2 qian, 4 fen, and 7.5 li, and medium pattern was 2 qian, 3 fen, and 7.5 li. Black flower is out of stock, and it is difficult to find printed Zhigong Ni. Double Military Fine Twill has already left the customs for 10 taels. Zhigong Ni and Zhigong satin, if there are spot goods, are being shipped out every day. Therefore, it is difficult to predict the next step in the short term.

Metals: Tinplate Sells Well to Tobacco Companies

Yesterday, tinplate trading suddenly became brisk. For example, tobacco companies have suddenly greatly increased their purchases recently, so the standard price has suddenly risen. 90-pound English goods sold for 14 taels and 5 mace, 100-pound for 16 taels, 90-pound American goods for 16 taels, 100-pound for 17 taels, and 200-pound for 30 taels, zero 7 mace and 5 fen. It is said that over 1,600-700 boxes were opened in the market yesterday.
