The Problem of Implementing the Factory Law in Our Country by Chen Da

(1) General Remarks: (A) Origin of this study, the labor legislation of our country, its history is very short, regarding the factory part, in the eleventh year of the Republic of China, the Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce promulgated the Provisional Regulations for Factories by ministerial order. In the winter of the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, the Legislative Yuan promulgated the Factory Law. We feel that there are several places where the latter surpasses the former, which also indicates the progress of our country's labor legislation. However, regarding the National Government's Factory Law, there have been many discussions from various parties recently. Some believe that the intention of the law is very good, the purpose is to protect workers and promote the development of industry, and it should be implemented as soon as possible. Others believe that the law is close to ideal, and some articles are too far from reality, and must be amended before it can be implemented. In fact, the degree of reliability of these opinions cannot be determined without factual research. In February of the twentieth year of the Republic of China, the People's Livelihood Improvement Research Association (sponsored by the Christian Progressive Association) held a meeting in Shanghai and had a heated discussion on our country's Factory Law. As a result, a resolution was passed advocating for factual research with a fair and impartial attitude, and the author was appointed to undertake this work. Due to the constraints of time, personnel, and economy, the author took Shanghai as the initial research area. Although, to understand the truth of the facts, it is necessary to have a national scope. However, Shanghai is a region with particularly developed industry and commerce, and it is the region with the most Chinese and foreign factories. Therefore, the research in Shanghai is of course more important than other cities. From the research in Shanghai, we can see the general situation of the implementation of the Factory Law. At the beginning of the research work, several institutions cooperated and sponsored it. On the Chinese side, there was the Industrial and Commercial Management Association, and on the foreign side, there was the Employers' Association. Other sponsors included government agencies (such as the Nanjing Bureau of Statistics, the Industrial and Commercial Visiting Bureau, the Academia Sinica, the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau, etc.), public institutions, and labor unions. We are very grateful. (B) Scope of this study, the author engaged in stipulating a kind of investigation form. On the Chinese side, five investigators were sent to two hundred factories to fill out the form. On the foreign side, in both English and Japanese, the Employers' Association sought answers by correspondence and implemented the investigation. It took about a month to complete. In addition, there were talks with various parties, such as government officials and more than sixty Chinese and foreign employers (most of the foreign employers were handled by Ms. E.M. Hinder), more than ten labor union leaders, and more than ten male, female, and child laborers. Therefore, this study is largely based on the analysis of facts. It includes 176 Chinese factories and 52 foreign factories, with a total of 51,960 male workers, 1,041 female workers, 11,895 child laborers, and 3,173 apprentices. The industry is divided into six major categories, as shown in the following table: "Type of Industry" "Number of Factories" (1) Textile Industry 128, (A) Cotton Spinning Industry 49, (B) Cotton Weaving Industry 13, (C) Silk Reeling Industry 29, (D) Silk Weaving Industry 18, (E) Knitting Industry 19, (2) Chemical Industry 34, (A) Bleaching and Dyeing Industry 13, (B) Soap, Glass, Matches, Cosmetics, etc. 21, (3) Food Industry 24, (A) Tobacco Industry 17, (B) Flour, Canned Food, Food, Soda, Seasoning, etc. 7, (4) Public Utilities (Electricity, Tram, Gas, Tap Water, Telephone, Public Buildings, Public Buses), (5) Machine Industry 24, (A) Steel Industry, (B) Appliances, Electrical Appliances, Utensils, Construction Industry, Shipbuilding Industry, (6) Paper Making and Printing Industry "1. Total 228. (C) Methods and purposes of this study, the investigation method used this time is usually called the sampling method. The sampling standards are as follows: (1) The selected factories must meet the definition of the Factory Law. (2) The selected industries must have considerable economic and social impact. (3) Among the three types of workers, male, female, and child, the selected factories must have at least two types. (4) The scope of the factory includes large, medium, and small categories. However, due to practical difficulties, the selected factories cannot fully meet the standards. This study took a total of two and a half months. Some materials were actually unavailable, and some materials were not collected due to the limitations of talent, economy, and time, so there are many regrets. The organization of the materials is also inevitably subject to errors. If readers can point them out, we would be extremely pleased. Although this survey is simple, it is the first attempt at a factual study of the Factory Law and also the first time for Chinese and foreign cooperation. We hope that others will be willing to conduct more detailed and extensive research on this issue in order to understand the truth about the implementation of the Factory Law throughout the country. The purpose of this survey is to study the degree of implementation of the Factory Law based on facts, that is, to find appropriate answers to the following questions: (1) What is the normal working time per day in Shanghai's industries? (2) Is it possible to abolish the night work of female and child laborers immediately? (3) What is the economic loss to industry when the Factory Law is implemented? In addition to economic loss, what are the important impacts? (4) Based on the current situation, what parts of the Factory Law can be implemented and what parts still need to wait for some time? (D) Conclusions and recommendations of this study, this study has partial answers to the above questions, and some have not been answered due to the lack of sufficient materials. Now, based on the collected data, we have organized and analyzed it and created a simple report for public discussion. For clarity, we take the Factory Law as the main body and present the important clauses in the following table. The table is divided into three parts: (1) What is the current situation regarding each article? (2) What does the Factory Law stipulate regarding this article? (3) What are the author's recommendations regarding this article? The simple conclusion is as follows:

Comparison of Factory Law and Actual Situation and the Author's Recommendations

Item Current Situation Provisions of the Factory Law Author's Recommendations

1. Factory Records 149 factories have records, 79 factories do not, but the records are simple. Records must have 15 items and be submitted to the authorities twice a year. Records must have 13 items and be submitted to the authorities at the end of the year.

2. Working Hours The working hours of industry range from 8 hours to 11.3 hours per day. As a principle, 8 hours per day, but can be extended to 10 hours in certain circumstances. 10 hours per day (applicable to female workers and young workers)

3. Night Work Prohibition Time Female workers after 6 pm and before 6 am (not prohibited) Child labor after 6 pm and before 6 am (not prohibited) Female workers are prohibited from working after 10 pm and before 6 am Child labor is prohibited from working after 7 pm and before 6 am. Female workers work 10 hours at night within three years (same as daytime) Child labor works 10 hours at night within three years (same as daytime)

4. Overtime Work Unlimited 2 hours per day or 36 hours per month According to the Factory Law

5. Rest Days An average of 2.6 days per month, 55 factories give pay, and 121 factories do not. 4 days per month with pay 2 days per month without pay

6. National Holidays, Festival Holidays, Annual Holidays An average of 14.4 days per year, some with pay and some without pay. 8 national holidays with pay According to the Factory Law

7. Special Rest Days Probably none From July to 15 each year with pay Postponed

8. Age of Young Workers Entering the Factory From 9 years old, 10 years old to 14 years old (the latter is in a few cotton yarn factories) 14 years old 12 years old, but the body must be (A) a certain height (B) Pass the examination by a doctor

9. Working Hours of Young Workers No difference from adult workers 8 hours per day Daytime work (same as nighttime) 10 hours within two years, Daytime work 8 hours education 2 hours after two years, Nighttime work 10 hours until the abolition of night work

10. Compensation and Subsidies

A. Injury due to work Generally there is compensation, but the amount is inconsistent Within 6 months of injury, equal to two-thirds of wages, then equal to one-half of wages, limited to one year According to the Factory Law

B. Permanent Disability Generally there is compensation, but the amount is inconsistent Subsidy equal to one to three years of wages According to the Factory Law

C. Death Generally there is compensation, but the amount is inconsistent Two years of wages plus a pension of 300 yuan According to the Factory Law

D. Funeral Expenses There is probably a subsidy 30 yuan According to the Factory Law

E. Illness due to work Sometimes a small amount of subsidy is given Same as injury due to work Subsidy must be paid, but limited to industrial diseases

F. Medical Expenses Sometimes a small amount of subsidy is given Subsidy must be paid According to the Factory Law

11. Education 55 factories have educational facilities 10 hours to 16 hours per week limited to 16 years old According to the Factory Law, implemented two years later, limited to young workers and apprentices from 12 to 15 years old

12. Maternity Leave Each mother receives about 16.02 yuan 8 weeks of leave with pay 4 weeks of leave with pay, implemented one year later, limited to female workers who have worked in the factory for one year or more

13. Bonus 177 factories give bonuses, 35 factories do not. Bonus or distribution of profits Bonus equals 4% of wages

14. Safety and Hygiene Many factories do not have perfect equipment The regulations are not practical There must be practical regulations and they must be implemented immediately

15. Payment of Wages Once or twice a month, sometimes wages are deducted as fines Twice a month, wages may not be deducted in advance, overtime wages are one-third higher than normal wages According to the Factory Law

16. Wage Principles According to the supply and demand of labor The minimum wage rate is based on the living conditions of workers in the area The government appoints a minimum wage committee to investigate the cost of living in various places and then decide on the wage principles

17. Work Contract 81 factories have written contracts, 130 factories do not. If dismissed without prior notice, give the full amount of wages for the notice period Give 15 days' notice in advance or give wages equal to 15 days' wages

18. Factory Meeting No implementation Give discussion and other powers Limited to discussion with the main purpose of mutual communication between labor and management

19. Apprentices Generally, the treatment of apprentices is not good Apprentice contract According to the Factory Law

The above table is the final conclusion of this study. From this, the following conclusions can be drawn: (1) The study is far from the facts and is difficult to implement. (2) But the author believes that the Factory Law is a necessary law for social improvement. We must work towards this direction. (3) Therefore, we should take the Factory Law as the goal, but before reaching this goal, we must find a way in. The author does not presume to believe that several suggestions are the way in, because these suggestions are based on facts and are moving towards the Factory Law. If these suggestions are the way in, then we can implement the Factory Law in stages. Some clauses can be implemented now, and some clauses can be implemented after one year, two years, or three years. Now, a brief description is as follows: Implementation procedures of the Factory Law: (A) Implemented immediately: (1) Factory Records: (A) The factory shall maintain records in accordance with the Factory Law, deleting the workers' character, skills, work efficiency, and causes of illness. (B) This record shall be available for factory inspectors to consult at any time. (C) The factory shall report to the government once at the end of each year, and the report shall contain a summary of the records. (D) Add a disaster report to the record. (2) Young workers: All men and women who are 12 years old, a certain height (standard determined after investigation), and whose bodies have passed the doctor's examination, shall be issued an employment certificate. This doctor shall be appointed by the government. (3) Rest days: Two days per month (without pay) (4) Working hours: 10 hours per day (or 20 hours per day and night) This article does not apply to the following: (A) Seasonal industries (but the silk industry is not an exception), (B) Industries whose machine work is continuous and cannot be stopped (listed), (C) Those who use only male workers, (D) In case of natural disasters or special events, (5) Subsidies and Pensions: (A) The articles on injury and death shall follow the original text, (B) Add subsidies for industrial diseases (industrial diseases must be defined), (C) Delete sickness compensation, (6) Holidays: National holidays, 8 days per year, with pay, (7) Safety and Hygiene: As soon as more practical regulations are promulgated, they shall be implemented immediately, (8) Apprentices: Follow the original text, (9) Bonuses: The factory shall give bonuses at the end of the year, at least equal to 4% of wages, (10) Labor-management discussion organization (factory meeting): In order to promote labor-management goodwill, both parties shall elect representatives to discuss various issues related to labor and management. Of the above items, only three are related to economy, namely (A) 10-hour work system, (B) 8 days of vacation per year, (C) Bonuses, so there seems to be no major difficulty for immediate implementation. (B) Implemented one year later: Female workers who have worked in the factory for more than one year shall be given four weeks of leave with pay if they encounter childbirth and are certified by a doctor. (C) Implemented two years later: (1) Young workers work 8 hours per day, (2) Young workers and apprentices receive 2 hours of education per day. (D) Implemented three years later: Female workers and young workers are not allowed to work night shifts. After three years, the entire Factory Law will be discussed in detail. (E) Implemented five years later: (1) Rest days, four days per month, (2) Raise the age of young workers, (3) Increase the number of female factory inspectors, (F) Clauses to be postponed: (1) Wages, (2) Special rest days, (3) Work contract, (4) Sickness allowance, (5) Factory meeting. Why should the Factory Law be implemented in stages? There are two main reasons: (1) The implementation of the Factory Law places an economic burden on industry (such as shortening working hours, prohibiting female and child laborers from working night shifts, rest and vacation, maternity allowance, etc.). If these articles are implemented at the same time, I am afraid that the industry cannot bear it. Our country's industry is now in a dangerous position. There is international competition externally, and there are various difficulties in management and labor internally. If a heavier economic burden is added, it will be difficult to develop industry. Therefore, we advocate implementing the Factory Law in stages. For example, in the first year, industry will suffer losses due to shortening working hours. Therefore, the maternity allowance will be implemented in the second year, and so on. (2) There are several clauses in the Factory Law whose implementation must be prepared. For example, prohibiting female and young workers from working night shifts is impossible at present. Because cotton spinning, cotton weaving, silk reeling, and silk weaving industries use a large number of female and young workers. If they are suddenly prohibited, these industries will have great difficulties. Therefore, we advocate abolishing the night work of female and young workers three years after the implementation of the Factory Law. Finally, where should the way in begin? Since we take the Factory Law as the goal, the Factory Law does not need to be revised. The implementing regulations are based on the Factory Law, so they do not need to be revised either. The starting point is the order of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce regarding the temporary measures for certain clauses. It can be stipulated by ministerial order, because the situation of industry and labor is constantly changing, so the ministerial order can also change accordingly. This seems to be the most flexible method. In this way, the Factory Law is the goal of social improvement, and the order of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce is the starting point for realizing this goal.

Letter

Dear Sir, Having read the local news column of your newspaper, which stated that Chinese police officer No. 78 of our police station stopped a ferry from carrying passengers across the river at the Qichang Wharf, almost causing a major disaster, etc., this is inconsistent with the facts. Chinese police officer No. 78 of our police station was patrolling the Qichang Wharf in Pudong by boat at nearly 6 am on the 29th of this month. Later, he saw that the deck of the ferry at the wharf was loaded with more than 100 passengers, exceeding the customs regulations and endangering the safety of the passengers. He stepped forward to stop it and ordered the number of passengers to be reduced before opening. However, the owner of the ferry, Chen Songtao, not only refused, but also gathered a crowd to beat the police officer. The police officer was outnumbered and could not call for help in time. Later, a patrol boat from our police station passed by. Chen Songtao and others stopped when they saw the patrol boat from our police station. The patrol boat did not come to the rescue because it had other important business and did not know about this major change. The police officer took the opportunity to escape to the sampan he had originally taken and tried his best to escape. However, Chen Songtao ordered the ferry to chase back Chinese police officer No. 78. At that time, our police station had received information and sent people to rescue him from danger. Chen Songtao claimed to the passengers, "I am doing this for your benefit, so you should come out and help," and instructed the passengers to swarm and occupy the patrol boat of our police station. After many attempts to persuade them to leave, they were taken to the Customs Shipping Office, and the land police explained the situation in many ways before they dispersed. This is the real situation of what happened. Your newspaper's news has completely erased the facts. Chinese police officer No. 78 has been examined in the hospital, and the hospital has issued an injury report as evidence. In addition to filing a lawsuit with the court according to law to punish the perpetrator, we hereby send a letter to request a correction. Sincerely, to the editor of the Shanghai Shenbao. Sincerely, the New Customs Water Police Station. July 30th.

Dear Sir, Having reviewed the news on the Two-Road Defense Conference published in today's newspaper, the point on the distribution of internal defense is inconsistent with the facts. We hereby send a letter to request a correction. Sincerely, to the Shenbao. Sincerely, the General Staff Office of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters.

Youth Forum

Neighbors

— Ke

Just finished supper, everyone was gathered around the dining table chatting and laughing.

"Excuse me, gentlemen, is Mr. Jiang home?" A woman's face was reflected on the glass window.

The light in the room was dazzling, and the woman's face standing in the darkness could only show an outline, as if there was a man's shadow behind her.

"Mr. Jiang? He lives next door," my sister replied.

She thanked them upon hearing that, and went next door. Soon, the door of the dining room opened slightly, and she and a man in his thirties, short in stature with a fierce glint in his eyes, walked in.

"Mr. Jiang is out. This address, thank you, give it to him when he comes back."

Her swollen, pale face showed a humble smile. She extended her chicken claw-like hand, took a slip of paper from the man's hand, placed it on the table, and said to my sister,

She seemed to be around thirty years old, with long hair combed back neatly, and a cheap rhinestone clip from the department store in her hair. Her cheongsam was long and wide, and the hem kept swaying as she walked. The man was wearing a white gauze gown, constantly stroking the short, curly hair on his forehead, his eyes darting swiftly around.

"Thank you for agreeing to my request," the man said, his eyes darting around again. "You're welcome," my sister replied with a smile. They walked out humbly.

"Hmm, Zhang... his accent sounds like he's from our hometown," I said, picking up the piece of paper from the table.

The next morning, there was a rumbling of cars and noisy voices outside the gate. I went to the window to look out and saw the couple from last night moving in with many children, boxes, and furniture, dragging everything along.

The oldest boy, about ten years old, was dragging a pair of worn-out shoes, his upper body naked, his thin arms like withered branches, holding a suckling infant with sores all over its head all day long. His tired eyes and gaunt cheeks seemed to indicate he would never have the joy of a lively childhood.

My sister stood at the entrance of the dining hall.

"The weather is really bad, it's always raining," the newly moved-in woman seemed to be greeting my sister, holding the suckling infant in her arms.

Her collar was open, exposing a sunken chest, showing a sense of weariness from life.

"Yes, it keeps raining like this. I'm afraid this year will be a year of famine," my sister said, moving closer to her.

"Where are you from? X province, right?"

"That's right. My husband is from X province, and I'm from Sichuan."

"Are these two your sons?" my sister asked, as the oldest child came over to hold the suckling infant.

"Yes. Those three are not mine, because my husband has another family," she said, nodding towards the three squalid children standing at the gate.

"Why didn't you see that one?"

"She gave birth to a baby and is in confinement."

"What does Mr. Zhang do now?" my sister asked.

"Him? He used to be a battalion commander, and later he worked in many government offices, and also..." she said happily, but suddenly Mr. Zhang came back from outside, glanced at her, and she slowly stopped talking and walked silently into her room.

There were ten of them in total: the couple, six children, and a nanny, all living in one side room. Standing at the entrance of the dining room, we could see their room's furnishings completely.

A long white wooden table was placed by the window, and against the wall was a black, oily square table and two broken wooden chairs with missing armrests. Inside, several small iron beds were vaguely visible, cluttered and messy. The room was dirty and disorderly.

Mr. Zhang was busy hanging something, hanging it on the wall in the middle of the black, oily main table. He slowly lowered it with his hand, gradually revealing a half-length portrait of the Premier.

"Underneath it should be his will," I thought.

He then nailed a blue paper scroll under the portrait. Indeed, it was the will. Then, on both sides should be—"The revolution has not yet succeeded, comrades must still strive on"—this couplet.

Indeed, he hung them all up as before, but there was no Party flag crossed.

One day, we were having lunch when a scolding tone came from the side room next door.

"What do you want to eat? Is this kind of dish not to your liking? If you don't eat, then don't eat it!"

Mr. Zhang was sitting by the window, with preserved eggs, smoked fish, a bowl of steaming braised pork, and a glass of wine in front of him, the glass filled with deep yellow wine. He sipped his wine slowly, watching inside and scolding, but not as if he was angry, more like a leisurely form of entertainment.

"I know, what to eat? You eat fish, eat meat, and drink wine," she coughed twice, spat, and said, "But we women only have this salty pickled vegetable. What we wear and use, isn't it all brought by me? You heartless man!"

"Conscience? What conscience? If I had a conscience, I wouldn't have remarried," Mr. Zhang sneered.

"This, this is..." her voice gradually faded, "Heartless man, how did you entice and deceive me in the beginning, but now..." She was crying, her voice so blurred that it was indistinguishable.

"Forget it, is this a big deal? There are never good words in an argument," the nanny said softly, trying to persuade her.

"We always argue like this, wherever we are, it's always like this," Mr. Zhang said, seemingly proud.

"You better not interfere in this matter."

Indeed, Mr. Zhang had been here for six or seven days, and they had already argued more than ten times.

Although the rain had stopped, the dripping water from the eaves still sounded "drip, drip". The weather at the end of July was as cool as late autumn. I was reading a newly translated Norwegian play when the next door started arguing as usual.

At first, the sound was so low that it was unclear, but gradually the sound grew louder.

"Shameless, you should know how shameless you are!" Mr. Zhang shouted loudly.

"That's right, shameless, shameless. Anyway, I'm shameless. You cheated me, you cheated my family that there were no women, is that having a face?"

"Bandit, you are a bandit!"

This time, it was not as easy to calm down as before. The noise grew more and more intense.

"Bandit? Who is a bandit?" Mr. Zhang asked sharply.

"You, you are a bandit!"

"Okay, show me the evidence!"

"Kidnapping women, cheating money, isn't that a bandit? Evidence?" she laughed sharply. "I am the real evidence!"

Before she finished speaking, there was a loud bang, and the woman cried loudly.

"You hit me, you dare to hit me! Come on!" There was a crash, like the sound of a woman being knocked down.

"Bitch, hitting you, what about hitting you!" There were continuous sounds of hitting.

"Murder! Help!..." The woman screamed hoarsely.

The woman in confinement had a black crepe scarf tied around her head, her face pale and yellow, her frightened eyes constantly looking out the window.

Somehow, the woman broke free, desperately running out the door, like a captured mouse escaping the cat's mouth.

"Bandit, watch, I'm going to report to the police station! You..." she shouted, stumbling towards the entrance of the alley.

"What? You held me tight, but let her run to the police station? This is possible! She, she will be unfavorable to me!" Mr. Zhang pushed to the left and shrugged to the right, trying to break free from Mr. Jiang's hand that was holding him. Finally, he pushed away the people surrounding him and ran after the woman like a flying arrow. At this time, the number of people watching the excitement in the alley gradually increased, and everyone ran after them.

The sky was dark like ink, with thick clouds all around. The ground, which had just rained, had puddles of muddy water accumulating on the stone slabs, which were stepped on by many feet, making a "gurgling" sound. The muddy water splashed in all directions, like the spray of a fountain.

The group of people who had just run past in the mud ran back, this time running in front of the main character.

"I'll be beaten to death if I go back! I, I'm not going back!"

The woman struggled desperately, the collar of her clothes torn, with a crack down the middle, half of the front dragging to her knees, revealing a skeletal chest.

Mr. Zhang didn't say a word, tightly biting his teeth.

With one hand pinching her hands and one hand waving away the crowd, he ran straight in.

The woman was dragged involuntarily, her feet like floating on the ground, dragged into the gate. She screamed sharply.

"No, don't go in! I'd rather die outside!"

Mr. Zhang still didn't say anything, just dragging her in with force, his eyes shooting out a murderous look, as terrifying as a half-crazed beast.

"Help! I'll be beaten to death if I go in... no, don't go in! Help!..."

The woman screamed like a pig being slaughtered, her whole body thrown into the muddy water. The light from the dining hall shone on her disheveled hair, swollen eye sockets, and face smeared with blood, like a mud bodhisattva washed by rain.

A general feeling of anger, like it was about to burst through my chest, my brain, I couldn't help but shout, "Hit, hit, hit this bully of women!"

This sudden shout passed through everyone's faces like lightning, instantly igniting the flames they had been harboring, and all together, like a wave crashing against the rocks, they furiously condemned Mr. Zhang. Seeing that everyone was hostile towards him, he let go, and said with an unnatural sneer,

"Nothing, I didn't hit her, please rest assured."

…………………………

"Gentlemen, listen to him, he is a liar. He, he beat me so cruelly, look!" She slowly got up from the ground, lifted her trousers and sleeves, and blue-purple wounds were scattered on her bony limbs. She panted and said,

"Gentlemen, he is so cruel. He beat me until I'm sick, and I often cough up blood. Please judge fairly, gentlemen, should he be like this? He..."

"Ah, how can he be so cruel?" a middle-aged man said, shaking his head.

"In a fight, women are always weaker, but men should have some conscience," said Mrs. Qiu, who lived in the front house.

"I am also a husband, but I have never treated a woman like this."

"Yes, if all men were like him, the women in the world would probably be exterminated."

"Ah, it's rare to see such a fierce person."

"……………………"

"He... ugh..." The woman cried sadly and continued, "Alright, don't talk nonsense, the neighbors have been annoyed enough by our noise," Mr. Zhang said to her in a low voice, then smiled and greeted everyone,

"Sorry, we made a fuss. I'm very sorry, please everyone take a rest."

The people watching the excitement saw that things had calmed down and felt it was boring, so they dispersed.

The woman was dragged into the room by Mr. Zhang with a mixture of intimidation and coaxing. There was indeed no more beating that night, but the woman sobbed and cried like a ghost all night long.

The next day, the side room next door was empty, showing a kind of quiet atmosphere. We didn't see them again after that.

Later, I heard from the landlord next door - Mr. Jiang, Mr. Zhang's friend - that,

She was a widow. After her husband died, he left some property and a child. Mr. Zhang, because of his friendship with her deceased husband, took the opportunity to seduce her, saying that he had been a battalion commander, how rich his family was, that he had not yet married, how sincerely he loved her, and that he would always love her passionately—but later, after he used up her property, he would often beat her over a small matter. This time, I heard it was just because she wanted to buy four copper coins' worth of white sugar.

Guidelines for the Youth Garden Section

(1) The content of articles should be about the discussion of youth issues, news of schools or students at home and abroad, essays, descriptions of school life, and casual notes. The style is not limited.

(2) The content of drawings should be limited to youth issues.

(3) The content of photos should be qualified as youth life (such as sports, travel, tours, drama performances, gatherings, exhibitions, various competitions, etc.), school news, and youth movements. Both individuals and groups are welcome. Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(4) The number of words per article should not exceed 2,000.

(5) Write horizontally, do not write carelessly, Western languages should be omitted if possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

Whether or not the submission is published, it will not be returned. If you need it to be returned, please make a statement in advance.

(6) Do not write horizontally on the manuscript, do not write carelessly, Western languages ​​should be omitted if possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not use watercolor paints for drawings, and do not use colored paper, you must use black drawings on white paper.

(8) Please indicate that submissions should be sent to the Editorial Department of the Youth Garden.

(9) Whether or not the submission is published, it will not be returned. If you need it to be returned, you should declare it in advance.

(10) The remuneration for articles is divided into three types: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand words. The remuneration for each drawing and photo is also the same. If there are special manuscripts, the remuneration will be calculated separately.
